Details of the Riot by Japanese in Qingdao 73

Qingdao Correspondence on the 12th: Ever since the Northeast Incident occurred, Japanese residents in Qingdao have been creating disturbances and seeking quarrels daily, hoping to expand the incident and achieve their aggressive goals. Our side has long been aware of their intentions and has tried its best to make concessions in the face of events, so we have been able to live in peace. On the 9th of this month, the "Minguo Daily" published a report about the assassination attempt on the Japanese Emperor, with the headline "Korean Patriot Lee Hwok-so Attempts to Bomb Japanese Emperor Without Success." The Japanese residents then used this as an excuse to make trouble, believing it was an insult to the Japanese Emperor. They held a meeting the other day and sent representatives to meet with the Japanese Consul to protest to the municipal government, demanding that the responsible personnel of the newspaper be severely punished. This matter had not yet been resolved when several Japanese of unknown names broke into the Minguo Daily office at around 9:00 AM on the 12th. The security guard, Xu Yinghua, was unable to stop them. The Japanese went straight into the business department, and one of them threw a glass bottle containing explosives at the stove. With a loud bang, flames shot out in all directions. The glass shattered, and the doors, windows, and floor were burned. The newspaper office was thrown into chaos. They tried their best to put out the fire. The Japanese then fired more than a dozen shots from their handguns and rushed out the door. The police on duty, feeling outnumbered, did not dare to arrest them and allowed them to escape. After receiving the report, the Public Security Bureau immediately sent personnel to the scene of the incident to conduct a detailed investigation and reported to the municipal government, preparing to negotiate with the Japanese consulate. Unexpectedly, one wave subsided, and another rose. At 4:00 PM on the same day, the Qingdao City Party Headquarters was also burned by the Japanese. It seems that the Japanese felt that burning down the Minguo Daily was not enough to vent their anger. They held an emergency meeting at the Japanese Residents Group on Zhongshan Road at 3:00 PM on the same day. About 300 people attended. Four points were decided on the spot: (1) Dissolve the City Party Headquarters; (2) Close down the Minguo Daily; (3) Punish the president and editor-in-chief of the newspaper; (4) Mayor Shen must personally go to the Japanese Consulate to apologize. The above four points were sent to the Japanese Consul General to negotiate with the municipal government. After the meeting, more than a dozen thugs were sent, carrying handguns, wooden sticks, and bayonets, to provoke trouble at the Minguo Daily office first. By that time, the newspaper staff had already hidden themselves. The Japanese fired several shots to show their force and then left. They then went to the City Party Headquarters and rushed in, pouring oil and setting fire to the auditorium downstairs, intending to burn down the Party Headquarters. The Party members had received information and escaped. The Japanese fired more than a dozen shots upstairs and left in anger. In order to avoid escalating the incident, the municipal authorities only sent plainclothes police to monitor the actions of the Japanese secretly. Therefore, although the Japanese committed outrageous acts, there were no conflicts with the police. After receiving the report, the municipal government lodged a serious protest with the Japanese consulate, but the Japanese Consul did not respond.

It is heard that when the Japanese residents held a meeting, they also decided on a secret plan, namely to overthrow all organizations and groups that are unfavorable to the Japanese residents (such as the City Party Headquarters, the Minguo Daily, the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association of all circles, the Fishing Company, etc.), and to gather members of the National Essence Society to carry out riots. Once the incident expands, the Japanese Navy can use this as an excuse to land and carry out a plan to occupy Qingdao. It is heard that there are about 300 members of the National Essence Society who have gathered at the Japanese Residents Group and appear to be planning to carry out riots tonight. Therefore, the situation in the city tonight is extremely serious. European and American residents have received the news and are holding a meeting at the International Club to discuss preventive measures.

Qingdao Correspondence on the morning of the 13th: The riot by Japanese in Qingdao has been reported in yesterday's letter. The following are further details of the Japanese atrocities last night (12th):

▲ Burning of the City Party Headquarters: After the Japanese residents convened an emergency meeting and decided on riot measures, they proceeded according to the planned plan. First, they gathered more than 300 members of the National Essence Society and assembled at the Japanese Residents Group at 7:30 PM to await orders. At 8:30 PM, the members, all carrying handguns, wooden sticks, and bayonets, set off together. They first sent people to block all the roads and then piled up the pre-placed explosives downstairs in the City Party Headquarters. With a loud bang, a raging fire erupted. In less than half an hour, the flames soared into the sky, illuminating the entire city. Chinese and foreign residents were frightened and uneasy. The fire brigade heard the alarm and tried to rush to put out the fire, but they were all stopped by the Japanese National Essence Society members, who did not allow them to go. In order to avoid conflict and prevent the incident from escalating, the municipal government had no choice but to stand by and watch it burn. Fortunately, the City Party Headquarters staff and workers received the news in advance and escaped, avoiding a tragic end. The City Party Headquarters is located on Taiping Road, Nanhai Cliff, very close to the consulates of various countries such as Britain and the United States. The building is a four-story building, solid and spacious, and is one of the most numbered buildings in Qingdao (the house is the property of the Opium King, Liu Zishan, and is now owned by the government for use). There are hundreds of rooms up and down. The City Executive and Supervisory Committee and the First District Party Headquarters are located here, and the staff dormitory is also inside. This time, it was burned by the Japanese, and it has become a pile of tiles and debris. Only the surrounding stone walls stand tall, and the interior has been reduced to ashes. The total loss is estimated to be around 300,000 yuan.

▲ Vandalism of the Minguo Daily: After the Japanese rioters burned down the City Party Headquarters, they went to the Minguo Daily office on Zhongshan Road. The Japanese originally intended to burn the newspaper office to the ground, but because the newspaper office was in the downtown area and surrounded by Japanese houses, they were afraid of being affected, so they temporarily changed their plan. After the rioters arrived at their destination, they rushed in and vandalized the newspaper's business department, editorial department, movable type department, and printing department. All the lead type racks, printing machines, doors, windows, and tables and chairs were smashed to pieces and scattered on the ground, making it a horrible sight. All the items in the staff dormitory on the third floor were also vandalized and left in a mess. When the newspaper office was vandalized, there were police officers on duty all around, but they did not dare to interfere because they were afraid of the Japanese violence.

Qingdao Correspondence on the afternoon of the 13th: There are two Japanese warships anchored in Qingdao, the Izumo and Yakumo. Last night (12th), when the Japanese set fire to the City Party Headquarters, the warships used searchlights to illuminate the streets of Qingdao. At around 10:00 PM, the landing parties of the two warships, about 600 men, landed armed on the front sea, ostensibly to protect the Japanese consulate and Japanese residents. Some were stationed near the Japanese consulate on the front sea cliff, and some were stationed to the left and right of the Japanese Residents Group on Zhongshan Road. At that time, important roads were blocked, traffic was cut off, and they were armed with live ammunition, as if facing a formidable enemy. At around 12:00 AM, a Russian man passing through the Japanese military-controlled area on the front sea cliff was stabbed several times by Japanese soldiers with bayonets. He was seriously injured and was taken to Qingdao Hospital for treatment. Their barbaric situation can be seen. Only at dawn did the Japanese soldiers on Zhongshan Road retreat to the Japanese Residents Group. Traffic in the city was restored, but the posts near the Japanese consulate were never withdrawn, and several sentries were stationed on the roof of the consulate for lookout. However, the Japanese soldiers have not clashed with the local police.

After the Japanese residents burned down the City Party Headquarters and vandalized the Minguo Daily, they still felt it was not enough. At 10:00 AM this morning (13th), they sent 23 representatives to the municipal government to request to see Mayor Shen Honglie. Secretary-General Hu Jiafeng met with them on his behalf and asked their intentions. The representatives made many unreasonable demands. Hu replied that if they had any opinions, they could directly express them to the consulate of their country, and the consulate would then negotiate with the municipal government. The government was not in a position to discuss directly with the representatives. After about two hours of conversation, they dispersed without results. At 3:00 PM, the Japanese residents held another emergency meeting to discuss expanding the incident and how to proceed. The content was highly confidential. It is heard that there were several items: (1) Eliminate all news organizations in Qingdao (according to the Minguo Daily method); (2) Vandalize the Fishing Company (because it hinders Japanese fishing) and the Exchange, and domestic goods malls; (3) Dissolve the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association, etc. After the meeting, more than a dozen representatives went to the municipal government at 5:00 PM to see Mayor Shen. The results are unknown, but according to Japanese sources, Mayor Shen has negotiated a peaceful resolution with Japanese Consul General Kawagoe, stationed in Qingdao. The conditions are as follows: (1) Regarding the Minguo Daily's report on the incident, the municipal government will issue an official document to the Japanese consulate expressing regret and seriously warning Chinese newspapers to pay special attention to future reports related to the Japanese Imperial Family in order to maintain friendly relations; (2) Liu Youting, the president of the Minguo Daily and a standing committee member of the Party Headquarters, will personally visit Consul General Kawagoe at the Japanese Consulate General to express regret for the inappropriate report and prove that similar incidents will never happen again in the future; (3) The municipal government will order the Minguo Daily to suspend publication for ten days and suspend the editor-in-chief of the newspaper; (4) After the Minguo Daily resumes publication, it will publish a statement acknowledging the inappropriateness of the report and admitting its mistake. As for the Japanese rioting and burning of the City Party Headquarters, the municipal government will file a negotiation with the Japanese consulate for separate handling.

Japanese Consulate in Fujian Pressures Chinese Newspapers 74

▲ The Provincial Government Actually Grants Its Request to Seal the Newspaper and Arrest People

Fuzhou Correspondence: The Sino-Japanese negotiations that have occurred in Minyuan in recent days have been reported in the previous newspaper. Unexpectedly, on the 9th of this month, the Japanese Consul again pointed to the "Oriental Daily" and the "New Tide Daily," stating that the reports and comments on the assassination of the Japanese Emperor contained insults and ridicule of the Japanese Emperor. He used the telephone to threaten the provincial government, saying that the officers and soldiers of the Japanese fleet stationed in Fujian were extremely indignant at the reports and were about to send all armed soldiers to the shore to demonstrate. He said that he was now trying his best to dissuade them. He said that if the provincial government did not take action against the two newspapers within two hours, the consul would not be responsible for the safety of Fuzhou. His tone was extremely strong. After receiving the phone call, the provincial government immediately convened a joint meeting of the Party, government, and military to discuss countermeasures. As a result, the "Oriental" and "New Tide" newspapers were ordered to suspend publication, and Wu Changming, the president of the "New Tide" newspaper, was sent to the Public Security Bureau for questioning. After the meeting, they also used the telephone to reply to the Japanese Consul. In the afternoon, they convened a meeting with news reporters, and Lin Zhiyuan, the provincial committee, reported the course of the negotiations, and ordered all newspapers to submit news drafts regarding Japan to the Garrison Headquarters for review before they could be published to avoid causing negotiations. Newspaper reporters said that since the Northeast Incident, the "Minbao," which was run by the Japanese in Fuzhou, had also published many insulting reports about the Chinese authorities. For example, before Chiang Kai-shek stepped down, he was even called a tyrant and deserved to be torn apart by five horses. Insulting the head of state of the country in this way, the provincial government did not say a word to correct it. However, a domestic newspaper slightly criticized the head of state of another country and was severely punished with suspension of publication and detention. This was an unprecedented initiative and caused deep indignation. Some extreme people said that since freedom of speech was so restricted, it would be better to suspend publication altogether to avoid the provincial government being responsible. The discussions were varied and inconclusive (February 11).

The Japanese Government Publishes the So-Called "Sino-Japanese Secret Agreement"? 75

The "Sino-Japanese Secret Agreement" recently promoted by the Japanese side has been firmly denied by our country's diplomatic authorities. According to the Japanese Dent Agency, the Japanese government said that regarding the Treaty on the Restoration of Manchuria and its attached agreement, which were concluded in December of the 38th year of Meiji (1905), Japan had specifically requested that the restrictive matters be inserted into the main clauses. The Qing side decided not to announce them due to internal relations. There were 16 of these restrictive matters. However, there are many misunderstandings in the public about the existence of the secret agreement, and some important Chinese figures have denied it. Recently, Chinese news carried the official denial message from the Chinese authorities. The Japanese government, in response to the Chinese side's denial, today (15th) publicly released the full text through the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. The content is as follows: (1) The railway between Changchun and Jilin will be funded by the Qing country, but if the funds are insufficient, it must borrow from Japan, and the amount must be about half of the total amount of funds required. The loan contract shall be negotiated in accordance with the loan contract between the Qing Imperial Railway Bureau (Shanhaiguan Nei Wai Railway Bureau) and the Qing-British combination. The loan term is 25 years, and it will be repaid annually in installments. (2) The military railway laid by Japan between Fengtian and Xinmin will be sold to the Qing country by commissioners appointed by the two governments to fairly agree on the price. The Qing country will rebuild it into a self-operated railway. In addition, the amount of funds required for the line east of the Liao River must be invested by Japanese capital and repaid annually in installments within 18 years. The loan contract shall also be negotiated in accordance with the loan contract between the Beiqing Imperial Railway Bureau and the English-Qing combination. Military railways in other places will be removed when the troops are withdrawn. (3) The Qing government, for the purpose of protecting the interests of the South Manchuria Railway, shall not lay other main lines or branch lines of railways close to or parallel to the railway that may hinder the interests of the railway before the railway is recovered. (4) The Qing country must make Russia faithfully and strictly implement the Qing-Russian Treaty on all railways in North Manchuria and take full measures. If Russia violates the provisions of the treaty, the Qing country must make a serious protest for the sake of correction. (5) In the future, when Japan and Russia continue to negotiate the start of railway business in accordance with the provisions of Article 8 of the Treaty of Peace between Japan and Russia, Japan must notify the Qing country in advance. At this time, the Qing country must inform Russia through the commissioners dispatched by the country, expressing that it must participate in the negotiation, and participate only after Russia recognizes it. (6) With regard to the mines in the Fengtian Province surrounding the railway, regardless of whether they have been mined or not, a fair and detailed regulation shall be formulated for mutual compliance. (7) Regarding connection operations, telegraph lines in Fengtian Province, and submarine telegraph lines between Lushun and Yantai, general related matters may be handled by the two countries through consultation at any time if deemed necessary. (8) The regulations on opening up various places in Manchuria shall be made by the Qing country itself, but it must consult with the Japanese Minister in Beijing in advance. (9) If the Russian side does not object to the navigation of Japanese ships on the Songhua River, the Qing country should recognize the navigation. (10) After the troops of Japan and Russia withdraw from Manchuria, the Qing plenipotentiary committee, for the sake of guaranteeing the sovereignty of the Qing country and the peace of the place, must take sufficient administrative measures, and for the sake of promoting benefits and eliminating malpractices, it should earnestly strive to restore peace. On the one hand, it is declared that the Qing government will fully protect the safety of life and occupation of all foreigners residing in the region, but the Qing government will take appropriate measures to settle the matter regarding the restoration of order. (11) If the Japanese plenipotentiary committee has military necessity, the Qing government shall notify the Japanese government in accordance with the purpose of the declaration to take action against the Japanese subjects residing in Fengtian. On the one hand, in order to enhance friendly relations between the two countries, the two governments shall take appropriate measures to prevent future interference in the administration of the Qing country or damage to public and private property. (12) Before the Japanese troops withdraw from Manchuria after the restoration of peace, if governments interfere in the administration of Qing local officials or damage Qing public and private property by exercising rights due to military occupation, according to this declaration, the two governments shall jointly estimate and compensate the losses fairly. (13) When Qing local officials want to send troops to suppress bandits before the Japanese troops have completely withdrawn from the place, they must consult with the Japanese military commander stationed in the place in advance to avoid misunderstandings. (14) The Japanese plenipotentiary committee shall not, before the withdrawal of troops, interfere in the local administration of the Qing country without reason or leave the railway zone without permission with regard to the railway garrison between Changchun, Lushun and Dalian leased land boundary lines. (15) Before the Japanese troops withdraw, the Qing local officials in Yingkou shall not enter the area without authorization to handle official duties. The date of appointment of Qing officials shall be determined after this treaty is finalized, but the Japanese Minister in Beijing and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs shall quickly negotiate and decide on it. In the area, since there are still a large number of Japanese troops, the quarantine and epidemic prevention rules shall be agreed upon by the officials of the two countries to prevent the spread of immune diseases. (16) The income of the Yingkou Customs shall be kept in Yokohama Specie Bank and returned to the Qing country when the troops are withdrawn. The regular customs revenue of Yingkou and other local tax revenues shall be used as local expenses. The revenue and calculations shall be handed over to the Chinese local officials when the troops are withdrawn.

Japanese Forcibly Seize Xi'an Coal Mine 76

Beiping Correspondence: The Xi'an Coal Mine, which belongs to the Northeast Mining Bureau, is located northeast of Shenyang and is directly accessible by the Shenhai Railway, about 200 miles away from the provincial capital. It is a good coal mine in Liaoning Province and has long been coveted by the Japanese. It was previously operated by ten mining merchants separately. Five years ago, new shares were added. In addition to the original capital and loans, a total of 1.4 million yuan was used to expand the organization and rename it the Xi'an Coal Mining Company. However, the mining rights are still in the name of the various mining merchants. Later, due to poor engineering, the daily coal production was only 300 tons. In the spring of last year, the board of directors hired Wang Zhengfu as the general manager and continued to increase shares by more than 1 million yuan to raise funds for activities and focus on management and reform of work. The output was finally increased to 800 tons per day. New machinery was purchased and electricity was installed. On the one hand, convenience of transportation was sought, and the number of workers was increased to more than 5,000. It was expected that by the end of the year, the daily production could reach more than 1,000 tons. Unexpectedly, the September 18th Incident occurred, and transportation and finance were completely blocked by the Japanese. Under these circumstances, workers had to be dismissed and operations temporarily suspended. The company had no funds, so coal strips were used as collateral to develop Wang Zi. Until October 7th, former Japanese Colonel Kawamoto Daisaku, Wada Jiwei, police adviser of the Shenhai Railway Pseudo Committee, and Yasuda Yuzo, who was transferred from the Fushun Mine, led more than 20 armed Japanese people to the An Mine, claiming to be investigating, and tempted them with sweet words. The company side politely refused and had no room to take advantage of it. Except for Kawamoto Daisaku who returned to Shenyang City, the remaining Japanese people stayed on the street in the name of investigation. On the 16th, Kawamoto returned from Shenyang, leading all the Japanese people who stayed on the street and entered the mountain with great fanfare, directly claiming to take over the Xi'an Coal Mine, and followed a pseudo-industry office chief An to force the handover freely, intending to forcibly occupy it. At that time, the acting mine director of the mine, Fu, said that the company established with state capital should follow the formal procedures and the shareholders agreed before the handover could be sternly refused. They left in disappointment. Mining Director Fu knew that their ambitions were difficult to suppress, so he went to Shenyang intending to mediate, but he was met by Kawamoto, who sent him to the Japanese Military Police Corps and detained him for eight days before he was released. On the 28th, the Japanese forcibly occupied the Xi'an Mine, appointed themselves as the general manager, appointed Yasuda as the mine director, presided over the mine administration, and distributed more than 20 Japanese people transferred from the Fushun Mine to various affairs and seized it wantonly.

Twists and Turns in the Replacement of the Director of the Shandong Tax Audit Office by the Provincial Government 77

Jinan Correspondence: After the Shandong Provincial Government took over the national tax agencies such as the National Transportation Envoy, it appointed Chai Chunlin as the director of the Shandong branch of the Salt Affairs Audit Office to take over. The reason was that the audit office was established due to foreign debt relations, and he was dispatched by the Ministry of Finance. If the provincial government replaced him, he would have to ask the ministry for instructions. Therefore, he refused to sign the official documents that came and went. Chai Chunlin reported to the provincial government, and the provincial government telegraphed the Audit General Office for negotiations. Blake also telegraphed the General Office for instructions. Hunan Provincial Government Demands Funds from the Central Government 78

▲ The Short-Disbursed 600,000 Should Be Disbursed Promptly

▲ Increase Subsidies According to the Budget in the Future

Changsha Correspondence: The national and local taxes in Hunan Province have long been divided, with all the national tax revenue used as military expenses for the Fourth Route Army, and the unified tax, land tax, and deed tax used as administrative expenses. The military expenses have been short due to years of expansion, and the arrears have reached ten months. From January of this year, the military expenditure was reduced to 1 million yuan, and the salt tax increased by 2.5 yuan per package from January to replenish the military expenditure. There will be no more difficulties in the future. As for administrative expenses, since the unified tax was abolished last year, the reliable revenue of 700,000 yuan per month has suddenly decreased. Although business tax and production and sales tax are held, the total monthly revenue is only 300,000 yuan, which is not enough to compensate for it. The monthly subsidy of 200,000 yuan from the Central Government has not been disbursed for nearly three months, resulting in an accumulated deficit of more than 6 million yuan in the provincial treasury. Before the abolition of the Likin tax, the Fourth Route Army borrowed more than 5.4 million yuan in military expenses from the provincial treasury, which has not been repaid yet, so the administrative expenses are unusually exhausted. He Jian telegraphed the Central Government yesterday to present the difficulties and requested four points: (1) Please raise and remit the subsidy of 600,000 yuan from October to December of last year in full within one month; (2) Increase the subsidy according to the budget deficit; (3) Find a way to have the national treasury allocate and return the military expenses; (4) Fully grant the province and local authorities the right to tax. The original telegram is recorded as follows: National unification, political renewal, and finance are the source of all administrations. It depends on internal and external maintenance to lay the foundation of the country and seek construction. Hunan is located at the crossroads of north and south and is particularly poor. Years of disasters and military disasters have made the people miserable. Since the division of national and local taxes in Hunan Province, all national taxes have been used for military purposes, and the monthly hardship is insufficient. Over the years, the provincial money has been used to borrow more than 5.4 million yuan, and requests for allocation have been fruitless. The provincial local tax revenue is often shorter than that of other provinces. Since the order to abolish the Likin tax was issued, Hunan Province first complied with the central government's tax reform purpose and abolished the unified tax, losing more than 8 million yuan in tax revenue each year. Unexpectedly, the central government has approved a subsidy of 200,000 yuan, which has been suspended for three months. The newly established business tax only collects more than 60,000 yuan per month. The total of land tax, deed tax, and other existing taxes is only more than 400,000 yuan. Moreover, disasters have occurred repeatedly, and tax sources have been exhausted. The current sales tax revenue maintains the food supply for various agencies. It is also exhausted abnormally. The expenditures have been tightened several times, from more than 1.69 million yuan per month to 1.1 million yuan. With the current revenue, the minimum recurring administrative expenses are also short of more than 700,000 yuan per month, and temporary expenditures outside the budget are not included. According to statistics, the provincial treasury owes more than 6 million yuan to various agencies for recurring expenses. The recent financial situation in Hunan Province has been reported to the departments and courtyards. In order to reform politics, provincial governance is particularly important to the national plan. I would like to give an overview. I hope that the central government will be aware of the province's financial crisis and kindly remit the subsidy of 600,000 yuan, a total of three months from October to December of last year, in full within one month. In the future, the rescue method should still be based on the divided standards and increase the subsidy for the local budget deficit in Hunan Province and remit it monthly. It will also be possible to allocate and return the borrowed military expenses, and give the province and local authorities the right to tax. However, in order to promote the abolition of malpractices in the constitutional government period, we should proceed with it fully so that the country can cope with the current difficulties. The Hunan Provincial Government Chairman He Jian and all members respectfully bow (January 13th).

Seven Stranded River Steamers Escape Danger 80

▲Location: Prince downstream of Anqing

Anqing correspondence: At Prince, sixty miles downstream of Anqing, since the onset of winter, the river water level has been dropping daily. The water level there is especially shallow compared to other places. Furthermore, the interwoven waterways and the surging waves have led to as many as seven Yangtze River merchant steamers becoming stranded there one after another recently. It is truly an unfortunate event for navigation. Investigations show that the merchant ships stranded there include Jiangxin of China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, Xin Ningxing, Yongxing, Fulong, and Songpu of Sanbei Steam Navigation Company, Pinghe of Jardine Matheson, and Wuxue of Butterfield & Swire, among others. The locations of the strandings were roughly the same. According to navigation industry sources, the strandings of the aforementioned merchant ships mostly occurred at night. The reason for this is that the drivers of each ship were occasionally inattentive, leading to accidents. Currently, the provincial government views these events as an unprecedented occurrence in the navigation industry. Additionally, the China Merchants Anhui Bureau and others have repeatedly requested protection. Therefore, the Anfeng patrol warship was dispatched to patrol and protect, and to find ways to transport passengers. When the warship arrived at the location, it was already late at night. Faint sounds of gunfire were heard intermittently from the shore, believed to be bandits lying in wait. The ship quickly moved forward, calming the people's hearts. Among them, the Xin Ningxing ship carried a larger number of passengers. Because the stranding lasted for a long time, the passengers made a great commotion towards the ship. The captain of the warship, Liu Wenyu, boarded the ship to comfort them and convey the Anhui provincial government's intention to provide protection. The turmoil subsided. Some foreigners on the ship were eager to leave. The warship first transported more than sixty passengers to Anhui, where they transferred to other ships to leave. Subsequently, the warship carried seventy members of the provincial government's guard regiment armed with pistols to protect. Liu Pengyi, the director of the Anhui Department of Finance, traveled downstream on the Jiangxin ship to Beijing to discuss Anhui's finances with the Ministry of Finance and then went to Shanghai to negotiate with Song Ziwen about the previous arrears of the cooperative loan. Liu then passed by the Anfeng warship. At 1:00 PM on the afternoon of the 11th, the Jiangxin ship was successfully towed out of danger by the Jianguo ship, and Liu resumed traveling downstream on that ship. The Yongxing ship also escaped danger on the same day. The Xin Ningxing ship escaped danger on the 12th. The Fulong and Songpu ships both escaped danger on the 13th. As of 1:00 PM on the afternoon of the 13th, all the stranded merchant ships had escaped danger one after another, and each set sail separately. The passengers were all safe and sound. It is also heard that the customs authorities have dispatched several survey ships to the river area to measure the water currents, mark dangerous locations with signs, and prohibit merchant ships from passing through at night and restrict overloading to prevent danger. (January 15)

Losses from Flooding in the Yangtze and Huai River Basins 81

▲Total losses estimated at 200 million yuan

▲Estimated disaster relief needs for farmers are 140 million yuan

Last year's floods spread throughout the country, with the Yangtze and Huai River basins suffering the most severe damage. After the National Government's Flood Relief Committee was established, disaster situation investigation forms were sent by the disaster area work group to the affected county governments for completion and reporting. Also, due to the excellent facilities of the Department of Agricultural Economics at Nanjing Jinling University and their extensive experience in agricultural surveys, they were specially commissioned to investigate the losses to agriculture and the situation and needs of farmers in the disaster areas of the Yangtze and Huai River basins. This investigation has now been completed, and the results can be summarized as follows:

(1) Scope of Investigation: This investigation included six provinces: Jiangsu, Anhui, Jiangxi, Hunan, Hubei, and Henan, covering ninety counties, two hundred and forty-eight locations, and two thousand three hundred and sixty-six villages, with eleven thousand seven hundred and ninety-one farm households. Jinling University first sent personnel to Yuezhou, Hankou, Jiujiang, Nanjing, Yancheng, Tai County, Qingjiangpu, Wuhu, and Yuanzhou to establish offices and train local investigators. After the training, they were dispatched to the selected severely affected counties to conduct household-by-household investigations.

(2) Disaster Losses: The population of farmers affected by the disaster in the Yangtze and Huai River basins is approximately equal to the entire population of farmers in the United States. The percentage of farmhouses in the disaster area that were washed away by the flood was 45%. The percentage of farmers who migrated elsewhere was 40%. The average depth of waterlogging in the countryside was approximately nine feet. Livestock losses were approximately 59%, and agricultural tool losses were 61%. Stored grain and fodder were completely washed away and no longer exist. Based on the above figures, the estimated losses suffered by farmers in all 121 affected counties in the Yangtze and Huai River basins can be categorized as follows: 867,000,000 yuan for submerged agricultural products, 470,000,000 yuan for houses, 135,000,000 yuan for draft animals, 115,000,000 yuan for agricultural tools, 79,000,000 yuan for stored grain, 68,000,000 yuan for clothing and bedding, 60,000,000 yuan for fuel, 54,000,000 yuan for furniture, 30,000,000 yuan for other livestock, and 15,000,000 yuan for feed. The total is approximately 1,897,000,000 yuan, with an average loss of approximately 451 yuan per farm household. Losses to dikes, roads, and winter agricultural products were not included.

(3) Estimated Urgent Needs of Farmers: According to the results of the investigation, the urgent needs of farmers are (1) clothing and food, (2) livestock feed, (3) grain seeds, and (4) materials for repairing houses. The approximate amounts are as follows: 503,000,000 yuan for food, 470,000,000 yuan for materials for repairing houses, 88,000,000 yuan for fuel, 56,000,000 yuan for clothing and bedding, 251,000,000 yuan for grain seeds, draft animals, and agricultural tools, and 94,000,000 yuan for other urgent needs. The total amount of these urgent needs is 1,462,000,000 yuan.

Closure of the Jiangsu Provincial Guard Corps Cadre Training School 82

Reason: Lack of funds

The Jiangsu Provincial Guard Corps Cadre Training School, which was previously approved by the National Government upon submission by Zhang Zhijiang, the Pacification Commissioner of Jiangsu, in conjunction with Ye Chucang, the former Chairman of the Provincial Government, to establish a training school in Yangzhou with a training period of six months and a regular monthly expense of 19,000 yuan, to be drawn from provincial funds, was suddenly suspended due to a lack of funds less than a month after its opening. At the time of the school's closure, a declaration was issued, stating, "The purpose of establishing this school was to enable the people of Jiangsu Province to combine with military force, so that the militia could provide effective protection for the people. After several months of preparation, the school was finally established. Now, with the approval of the Jiangsu Provincial Government, it is to be suspended due to lack of funds. The project has been abandoned halfway. Feeling deeply regretful, we are ashamed to face the people of Jiangsu. We hereby respectfully present the reasons for the school's establishment, the process of its suspension, and our hopes for the future to the elders and brethren of Jiangsu Province. The reasons for the school's establishment can be divided into three points: (1) It was for the sake of permanent pacification. The situation in Jiangsu Province is complex, with numerous ports and waterways. The areas bordering neighboring provinces are particularly prone to bandit activity. Although the existing pacification forces, consisting of four divisions, can temporarily suppress banditry, they are still insufficient for thorough purification. This is because bandit activity is unpredictable and comes and goes without warning. Relying solely on military force is not the fundamental solution. To achieve permanent pacification, we must seek the people's self-defense capabilities. This is one of the reasons for establishing this school. (2) It was for the purpose of cultivating self-defense talents among the people. The cultivation of the people's self-defense capabilities begins with training. Although people's militias have been organized in each county of Jiangsu Province, the quality of training varies greatly. In some cases, they are merely militias in name and are unable to provide protection. In the event of an incident, they are easily captured by bandits, and the local area is ravaged, leaving the people with nowhere to escape. Therefore, militia training is urgently needed. However, it is necessary to seek qualified instructors for training. It is not possible to assign them from one place, as they may not be familiar with the local conditions. Nor is it advisable to allow them to be hired freely, as the methods may vary greatly. It is better to gather talents from various places, and after training, send them back to their hometowns to handle local affairs. Local people handling local affairs will achieve twice the results with half the effort. Therefore, it was stipulated that each county and district should select outstanding members of the militia to be admitted to the school, provide them with basic military training, and send them back to their original places after six months to undertake training work, teaching them step by step, like passing a flame from one torch to another, so that all counties in the province can establish well-trained militias with strong self-defense capabilities, so that the people can rely on them in times of emergency. This is the second reason for establishing this school. (3) It was for the purpose of saving military forces and transferring them to national defense. The country raises troops for national defense. In the case of Jiangsu Province, there are no fewer than four divisions stationed in Jiangnan and Jiangbei. This is not a small number. Pacification is only a temporary measure. If every province needs troops for pacification, the cost will be enormous. Moreover, at a time when foreign powers are encroaching, Jiangsu Province is a vital area for coastal defense. In the event of an emergency, the entire army will inevitably be deployed to face the enemy. If the local militias are trained, not only will bandits be unable to rise up, but they will also be able to ensure the safety of the rear, so that the country will have no internal worries and the people will enjoy peace and tranquility. This is in terms of wartime. In peacetime, troops can be freed up to cultivate and defend the borders. If one province does this, the whole country can do so. This can curb the ambitions of large and fierce enemies. Wouldn't the results be even greater? This is the third reason for establishing this school." Based on the above three reasons, we consulted with the former Chairman of the Provincial Government, Ye, and obtained his consent. On one hand, we jointly submitted the plan to the central government for filing. On the other hand, we mutually encouraged progress in terms of both human resources and finances. As a result of these efforts, we were able to admit more than 600 qualified students in December of the 20th year and implement classroom training. This is a brief overview of the establishment of the school. We hoped that with continued training, the people of Jiangsu Province would be able to combine with military force, the militia would be able to provide effective protection for the people, and the pacification work would be completed once and for all. Unexpectedly, the Jiangsu Provincial Government was reorganized at this time. The new members, upon taking office, felt that the finances were difficult and decided to propose the suspension of the school. Although we wanted to maintain the school, we were powerless to do so, and the planned project was abandoned halfway. It is deeply regrettable. Jiangsu Province is a region with abundant wealth and a concentration of talent. Although it suffered from a disaster this year, its vitality will not be difficult to restore. We hope that enlightened and enthusiastic individuals will wait until the financial strength is slightly improved and continue this established plan in advance to plan this permanent peace for the local people. If it can benefit the people, why must the results be attributed to us? If this is the case, then although the school is temporarily suspended, its spirit is not lost, and there is still hope for revival. The goal is still high, and it will eventually be achieved. This is also our personal hope. We hope that the elders and brethren will give us their kind attention. This is our declaration." (January 13)

Requesting Allocation of U.S. Wheat for Disaster Relief to Assist in Dike Repair The Dike Repair Committee stated that last year's continuous rain caused a disaster, and lake water poured back into the inland rivers, causing the collapse of dikes in various areas. The flooded fields amounted to more than 300,000 mu. The disaster victims were in dire straits, and starvation was pitiful. In order to provide both short-term and long-term relief, a work relief plan was established to repair the dikes in the affected areas. The estimated cost of the project is approximately 300,000 yuan. In addition to raising funds from the Flood Relief Association and presenting a request to the provincial government to allocate 50,000 yuan from the road construction funds, the actual amount is still less than 100,000 yuan, which is insufficient for the project. More than 100,000 disaster victims are in urgent need of relief. Yesterday, a special request was made to General Yu Qia from the National Flood Relief Association to release 30,000 shi of U.S. wheat from the central government loan, so that Wuxi's work relief could proceed. Rong Zongjing and Qian Sunqing were designated to go to Shanghai to negotiate.

Changshu 86

Guard Corps Member Flees with Arms The local district offices were ordered last winter to organize a guard corps to defend the local area. Each district has now been established. On the 14th, Zhao Jinwen, a member of the 10th District Guard Corps of Dongtang City in the 3rd District, fled the day before, carrying a Mauser pistol and dozens of bullets. The district chief, Cao Bingxi, fearing that the guard corps member might cause an accident with the weapon, immediately telegraphed the county government, requesting that the county's public security bureaus and guard corps be notified to pay close attention. If anyone is found, they can be handed over to armed agencies for strict handling by the county.

County Government Borrows Grain from Various Business Owners Since the establishment of the new provincial government, funds have been tight, and the counties have been ordered to collect winter tax urgently. This county was assigned 140,000 yuan. However, this year's continuous rain caused a disaster, and the autumn harvest was reduced. Many farmers were holding back, because the rent they received this year was only 20-30% of previous years. As a result, grain taxes were also affected. After receiving the order to remit funds, the county scraped together 60,000 yuan in foreign currency to remit to the province, but there was still a large difference. The provincial government continued to issue repeated orders to urge the county government and the finance bureau to pay up, but they were unable to cope. Wang, the director of the finance bureau, once considered resigning. Now, the Public Association of Taxpayers of Land Property in this county was established. The county government then consulted with the association to ask various business owners to prepay the grain tax, with an interest rate of 1.2% per month. In the future, the borrowed funds could still be used to offset the grain tax. After the land property association passed the resolution, it contacted various parties and borrowed more than 50,000 yuan in cash on the 14th to remit to the province.

Zhenjiang 87

County Government Prohibits the Transport of Cash Out of the County The County Magistrate of this county, Zhang Peng, is planning to find ways to maintain the current tight money supply and sluggish financial situation. According to confidential reports, the banks in this port will transport a large amount of cash out of the county by train. If this is true, the market will be seriously affected, and the local area will be even more panic-stricken. In addition to telegraphing the station to detain the transport, he telegraphed the banks in this port to stop the transport quickly.

Jiangbei Woman Robbed of Association Funds Ms. Yin Gao, a young woman from Yangzhou, received 23 yuan in association funds in Nanbaoyan. Yesterday afternoon, while returning home and passing through Zhuanlun Gang, three robbers with box guns stopped and searched her, taking all 33 yuan of her association funds.

Yangzhou 88

Police Detain Bandits Who Sold Plundered Goods The detectives Mi Tiao, Shao Shigui, and Chen Yongzhao of the County Police Team arrested four bandits, Chen Shuan, Lu Shucai, Bian Wengao, etc., at two grass sheds located at the east of the Imperial Palace and behind the Public Security Bureau of Dongguan Street in this city on the afternoon of the 13th. Over a hundred pieces of stolen clothing and dozens of pieces of scattered silver ornaments were seized on the spot. The team interrogated them and they confessed that they had repeatedly robbed and pillaged in the northwest townships. Now, detectives have been dispatched to the northwest townships to inform the victims to come to the city to identify the stolen goods. Also, Yang Weilong, the victim from the Nandu Temple in the west township, was summoned to the city to confront the bandits on the night of the 12th.

Nantong 89

Prevent and Suppress Bandits Along the Coast The areas along the coast of Tonghai and Qi counties have recently been severely harassed by a large number of sea bandits. The provincial and county water and land police forces are conducting a joint suppression. The bandits are fleeing in boats with kidnapped hostages. The 18th Water Police Team has sealed off the ports of Langshan and Dagang to facilitate the prevention and suppression. The county government has also established a water patrol team, which is responsible for patrolling the river and suppressing bandits.

Provincial Order to Stop Unauthorized Inspections of Foreign Vessels When foreign vessels pass through the Yangtze River, disputes and negotiations have occurred due to military and police inspections. The provincial government has ordered the county government to stop unauthorized inspections. If inspections are necessary, they should be carried out in accordance with established practice.

Tongru Bandit Executed by Firing Squad The bandit Xia Zemin from Tongzhou and Rugao counties was arrested by the police team and sent to the county government for interrogation. He confessed to arson, robbery, and murder. After reporting to the provincial government for instructions, it was telegraphed on the 13th to escort the bandit to the execution ground and execute him by firing squad.

Intense Battle Between Police and Bandits in Songji Port A large number of sea bandits arrived at Songji Port, and according to reports, they had more than a dozen male and female hostages, who were waiting to negotiate ransoms. The provincial and county water and land police forces learned of this and went to suppress them. The bandits stubbornly resisted and fought fiercely for a long time before finally collapsing and retreating. The unescaped bandits Li Daochen, etc., were intercepted and sent to the Nantong County Government for interrogation on the 13th.

Gaoyou 90

The Miserable Conditions of Disaster Victims in the 11th District The Gaoyou Branch of the Shanghai International Famine Relief Committee previously sent Xia Tongchun to investigate the 11th District of Huxi. He saw that most of the disaster victims in the area had no clothes or food. Lamentations were everywhere, and many people died of starvation. Some committed suicide due to hunger and cold. The tragic conditions were unbearable to witness. He has now returned to the city to report to the committee. It is heard that personnel will be dispatched within the day to provide relief to help the disaster-stricken people.

Danyang 91

A Fratricide Case Occurs in Lingkou A male corpse was found beside the Xiaoxihe River in Henan, Lingkou. After rushing to the scene, the 8th Public Security Bureau of the area determined that the deceased was Chen Xixue, an associate of Yang Qinggeng, a bailiff of the county government. There were knife wounds on his head and face, and it was determined that he had been murdered out of hatred. The case has been reported and an inquest is requested.

County Government Captures Two Bandits The case of Yin Wenyu's home in Dazhuang Village, 2nd District, being robbed and pillaged and the homeowner being killed last year has been unsolved for a long time. The county government has now received a tip that the case was committed by Zou Xiaoshang, Sun Shilin, and Ding Changlin. County Magistrate Wang immediately dispatched plainclothes detectives to secretly arrest the bandits Sun and Ding. They were secretly interrogated once by He Cheng yesterday and temporarily detained. A strict arrest order has been issued for Zou Xiaoshang for questioning.

Shaoxing 92

Fire at Duanhetou Causes Multiple Deaths and Injuries On the afternoon of the 14th, a fire suddenly broke out at the Shentongxing Tin Shop on Zhuangyuan Bridge, Duanhetou, Shaoxing. Firefighters from various places rushed to the scene to put out the fire. For a time, the noise was deafening, and there was extreme crowding. The stone embankment of the Wang family along the river was in disrepair for many years and was pushed over by the crowd, causing a tragic incident with multiple deaths and injuries. Ding Xiaoyuan, Shan Ronggui, and Ge Tiansheng, three members of the Public Security Bureau's fire brigade, were crushed to death on the spot, with broken heads and feet. Those seriously injured included Shao Amao, Fu Ahua, and ten others. The dispatcher Chen Abing and the driver Datou of the Tianyi Dragon were also crushed to death. Dozens of other onlookers were injured. Afterwards, the Public Security Bureau transported the injured to Fukang Hospital and Shaoxing Hospital for treatment.

News

Simple Elementary School Measures in Hubei Province 93

In order to facilitate the implementation of compulsory education, the Hubei Provincial Department of Education has twice revised and approved the Hubei Provincial Simple Elementary School Measures. The 12 articles of the measures, which have now been approved and filed by the Ministry of Education, are summarized below: (1) The Department of Education will establish simple elementary schools (hereinafter referred to as simple elementary schools) in compulsory education experimental areas in order to promote compulsory education. (2) Simple elementary schools should enroll children around the age of 15 who cannot enter formal elementary schools. (3) Simple elementary schools will have three to four grades, using a two-part system, with students attending in shifts in the morning and afternoon. (4) The number of children in each grade of a simple elementary school will be temporarily set at 50 to 60. (5) The main subjects in simple elementary schools will be Chinese, arithmetic, general knowledge, and physical education. The curriculum standards will be formulated by the Department of Education based on the Ministry's primary school curriculum standards. (6) Each grade of a simple elementary school must have at least two hours (130 minutes) of instruction each day, for a total of 500 hours (30,000 minutes) per year. (7) Any child in a simple elementary school who can complete the total amount of time (2,000 hours) in four years will be considered to have completed compulsory education. (8) Simple elementary schools with two grades will have one principal and teacher. Those with three or more grades will have one principal and teacher and one or two teachers. (9) The school buildings of simple elementary schools should borrow local schools, temples, shrines, and all public places. (10) Simple elementary schools should, before the start of the school year, work with the local public security bureau or autonomous organization to investigate out-of-school children in the area and encourage them to enroll. (11) The standard for the allocation of simple elementary school fees will be determined separately. (12) These measures will be implemented from the date of approval and promulgation.

Efforts of the Zhejiang Provincial Rural Teachers' School 94

The Zhejiang Provincial Rural Teachers' School, located in Xianghu near Hangzhou, has been making unremitting efforts to improve its internal organization since Principal Huang Tongyi took office. The recent measures are particularly noteworthy, such as "National Crisis Propaganda," "Land Reclamation and Road Construction," "Academic Competitions," "Rural Surveys," "Additional Farmers' Education Centers," "Opening Women's Sewing and Weaving Classes," "Establishing Farmers' Lending Institutions," and "Inspecting Waterborne Diseases and Pests." These efforts have been intense. Some are carried out regularly in the surrounding villages, while others are cultivated and built by teachers and students in sections. As for "Literary Competitions," "Calligraphy and Painting Exhibitions," "Musical Performances," and "Party Principles Speeches," they have all been held in turn. In terms of promotion, special attention is paid to livelihood issues. Women's sewing and weaving training is added to the people's schools to increase income. Work-study programs are implemented in primary schools, with special skilled workers serving as instructors to enhance children's survival skills. In view of the frequent hookworm scourge among villagers, Dr. Hong, a researcher at the Zhejiang Institute of Tropical Diseases and Pests, was hired to come to the countryside to inspect and eliminate the major problem. The teachers and students of the school have been able to cooperate effectively. Huang has been involved in rural education for many years and has always instructed his students to devote themselves to hard work. Therefore, the future plan is to build the school into a large-scale rural academic institution to promote the development of rural schools in Zhejiang Province.

Important Telegram from the Student Union of Various Universities 96

▲ Urging Wang, Hu, Jiang, and others to jointly face the national crisis

The Shanghai Student Anti-Japanese National Salvation United Association issued the following important telegram yesterday regarding the current situation:

▲ Telegram Urging Wang, Hu, and Jiang to Quickly Unite (Salutations omitted) Ever since the violent Japanese invaded and the Northeast fell, our villages have been occupied. This was truly caused by the government's initial mistake of remaining calm, followed by the military's mistake of non-resistance. Now, as we stand at a critical juncture where the nation's survival is at stake, and the people are weary and frightened, it is fortunate that you gentlemen have jointly advocated for peaceful unification, sincere national unity, consistent resistance to external forces, and jointly facing the national crisis. However, upon examination of the facts, this is far from the truth. The so-called peaceful unification and sincere unity still harbor many hidden dangers and lurking obstacles. In terms of resisting external forces, there is no consistency, and in terms of facing the national crisis, where is the joint effort? We believe that you gentlemen have dedicated yourselves to the revolution. Serving the party is serving the country, and serving the country is serving the people. You would certainly not abandon the solemn position of leaders of the 400 million people and instead seek refuge as exiles in foreign lands. Nor would you abandon the lives and property of the 400 million people and disregard the brutal trampling by the enemy. If you wish to maintain the solemn position of leaders of the 400 million people, there is no other way but to save the country and protect the people. We, the students, have witnessed the urgency of the national crisis and the fervent emotions of the people. The situation is critical. We have heard that your attitude is somewhat extreme, delaying your return to the capital, claiming illness and seeking leisure, and showing no concern for the national crisis and the people's suffering. Is this truly your original intention of serving the country and the people? Although we dare not presume to fathom your profound concerns and shifting strategies, in the past, you gentlemen have advocated for the people through involvement in military work, uniting to save the country, or taking responsibility in the private sector. Now, you are acting inconsistently and contradicting yourselves. How will you gain the understanding of the people, and how will you defend yourselves? Moreover, you bear the heavy responsibility of the nation and are at the forefront of the party and the country. Why do you not establish merit before others and speak words that serve as laws for the world? Bearing grudges and violating national interests, alas, you gentlemen are finished. What more can be said? As the saying goes, do not pursue profit dishonestly, and do not avoid harm disgracefully. Upon hearing these two phrases, you should realize that you have no face to meet the people again. You should reflect on yourselves. Having deceived the people in the past and now abandoning them in the future, you should resolve to punish yourselves to appease the people even in the slightest. The ocean of regret is not far off; let your souls yearn for it. The whole country sympathizes and awaits your orders with urgency. (Remainder omitted)

Middle School Student Delegation Returns to Shanghai from Beijing 97

▲ Sun Ke Gives Detailed Responses on the Current Situation

The delegation of middle school students from this city who went to Beijing to petition has returned after eight days, since their arrival on the 7th. The details of the petition have already been reported in various newspapers. The delegation felt that the current situation was becoming increasingly serious, the rear-area work was strained, and they had a clear understanding of the current state of the government. Although the petition could not achieve satisfactory results, they decided to return with tears in their eyes. They took a fast train from Beijing yesterday morning at 10:00 AM and arrived in Shanghai at 5:00 PM yesterday afternoon. According to reporters from the Guoyu Xinsheng News Agency, in addition to telegraphing back the situation in Beijing from time to time, they also held a reception for news reporters in Beijing the day before yesterday, issuing a circular telegram and declaration on the current situation. That evening, they also sent representatives to the Central Party Headquarters to meet with Sun Ke, inquiring about the government's concrete policies on domestic and foreign affairs. The key points of Sun's response to the petition are as follows: (1) Regarding domestic affairs, first is the government's finances (which have reached the point of utter exhaustion). The government's monthly regular expenses, when offset against revenue, only have a surplus of six million. Just in terms of military expenses, eighteen million is needed each month. Revenue is less than one-third of expenditure. Regarding the suspension of interest payments on government bonds, the government has lost almost all collateral (such as the Financial Public Bonds, the Russian Boxer Indemnity, Customs duties, etc.). Therefore, the general business community in Shanghai insists on opposing it and threatens the government with a strike. These are a minority of money-minded people who sacrifice the country's future, which is extremely heartbreaking. He deeply hopes that the students will express their views on these capitalists after returning to Shanghai. Second, regarding the period before Wang, Jiang, and Hu return to Beijing, a Special Committee has been organized to decide on all major party and national affairs. (2) Regarding foreign affairs, there are currently three possible paths. The first is passive, which is non-resistance to Japan. This is a path of neither life nor death. The second is active, which is to go to war with Japan. However, this will provoke international antipathy because Japan is fighting without a declaration of war, and we do not want to be accused of disrupting world peace and become the public enemy of all nations. The third is severing diplomatic relations, which is a national mobilization to cut off all economic and political ties with Japanese imperialists. This is currently the only and final path. If so, the problem can be expanded to the point of becoming serious and internationalized, thus arousing international sympathy. Through this, we can use the power of foreigners to recover lost territories in the Northeast, just as the Washington Conference led to the recovery of Qingdao. Finally, the representatives asked that, given that China is in a situation where the various imperialist powers are dividing it up, and our government has no fundamental solutions and is only talking about severing diplomatic relations with Japan, what will we do about those who are attacking China? Sun replied that one solution can solve everything, and there is no need to worry. We can adopt international diplomatic means to disperse the imperialist powers' attacks. He also firmly stated that if this path does not work, he would simply resign and yield to someone more capable.

Free Talk

Talks by Butingzhai (Studio of Non-Resistance) & Weeds by Chucaofu (Weeding Man)

Creating the Chinese Nation in the Midst of Creation 127

The Chinese nation was not originally created successfully. The mission of creating the Chinese nation rests in the hands of modern Chinese people.

The formation of a nation seems to go through three stages:

The first stage: Each tribe acts for its own benefit.

The second stage: Each tribe helps each other.

The third stage: Each tribe unites as one and stands on a single front to face a common enemy.

The arrival of foreign invasion is the only touchstone for a nation. If we want to know whether a nation has been created successfully, we only need to observe its reaction when foreign invasion strikes, and everything will become clear at a glance.

What stage has the modern Chinese nation reached in its creation? Is it evolution or regression? In my observation, the Chinese nation has already reached the second stage. If it were not for the obstacles of warlords, it could immediately jump to the third stage.

At the time of the Ming Dynasty's downfall, the majority of the Chinese nation was still lingering in the first stage. When Beijing fell, Nanjing remained a bystander. At the Yangzhou and Jiading massacres, people from other places stood by and did not offer rescue. The Ming Dynasty therefore fell.

Yesterday in Shanghai, someone initiated assistance to the Northeast Volunteer Army, and last time, people from the Southeast raised donations to help the Heilongjiang Army resist Japan. These are all important facts in the history of the Chinese nation's development. These events prove that the Chinese nation has developed to the second stage. This time, the assistance to the Northeast Volunteer Army is even more significant because the Northeast Volunteer Army is purely the people's military force, which displays the true national spirit. People of the same ethnicity in various places helping each other with real strength is definitely a step further than empty sympathy.

However, we cannot linger in this stage, thinking that donating some money to help the Northeast Volunteer Army is enough to fulfill our responsibilities. The formation of a nation must involve unity in action. The people of the whole country must unite and stand on a single front with the Northeast Volunteer Army to struggle. Only then can the great mission of creating the Chinese nation be completed.

The non-resisting warlords are sinking in the lowest layer of the first stage. In their minds, there is only their personal wealth and family; where is the nation? Therefore, non-resisting warlords betray the national spirit, which means betraying the Republic of China. The people of the whole country should immediately rise up and stand on a single front with the Northeast Volunteer Army to eliminate the separatist warlords, drive out the tyrannical Japanese army, and restore the lost territorial sovereignty, so as to complete the great mission of creating the Chinese nation.

Anecdotes of Shen Peizhen 128

— Qing Yao

Shen Peizhen was from Hunan province. She was an old pioneer in the women's revolutionary movement, a fellow townsman of Huang Keqiang, hence she was hailed as a heroine. She was already famous in the early years of the Republic. Her appearance was not strikingly beautiful, but her manner was natural and unrestrained. Usually, she was rather introverted and rarely smiled, but during political discussions, she would often slam the table and stand up, her loud voice shaking the roof tiles. Even male figures dared not argue with her, some even becoming speechless. It's clear she was not like the demure, smiling women of today.

After the Xuantong Emperor abdicated, Wang Zhaoming and Hu Ying were released from prison. Hu, named Jingwu, was also from Hunan. Initially, he became acquainted with two women while in prison. Afterwards, he married them, with Song Jiaoren as the officiant. This was widely circulated as a romantic tale, and various newspapers in Beijing praised it. However, Shen, upon hearing this, believed it damaged the dignity of women. She went directly to the wedding venue, confronted Song, and slapped his face with her palm, making a resounding noise. It became a laughingstock. But Song ultimately could do nothing to Shen and could only endure it. Later, some people said that Song's ambition to be in charge of industrial affairs never came to fruition was due to the force of this one slap.

Later, a member of the Guangdong Tongmenghui, Ye Xiasheng, pointed out that Hu had married two women and held the weddings on the same day, making them equal wives. He cited the "crime of bigamy. Whether according to the old or new laws, there are specific clauses. A man with multiple wives is a disgrace to civilized countries. Yet Hu Ying, a founding member of the Republic, should set an example with his every action. He openly committed bigamy in the capital, in a prominent area where foreigners could see, blatantly violating the law. From the President (at the time Yuan Shikai) down to the people of the whole country, no one seemed to notice his violation and offer any admonishment. Instead, various circles congratulated him and held banquets. What of the national law? What of human morality? What will foreigners think of our laughter and criticism?" He submitted a letter to the Beijing press association warning about this situation. Although the letter bore Ye's name, it was actually Shen who prompted it to help her speak out.

When Li Yuanhong became President, Shen was still lingering in Beijing. It was rumored that she went directly to the Presidential Palace naked to request a meeting. Huang Pi, fearing this, refused her. She insisted on requesting an audience, and he had no choice but to see her. She wore a large cloak, and her manner was composed. It was unexpected that she would ask for something. Moreover, it was an excessive amount, which he could not possibly provide. Shen then flung open her cloak, intending to harass him. Huang Pi was extremely embarrassed and immediately gave her 20,000 taels of gold. Only then did Shen leave. A certain member of the Guangdong Provincial Assembly was seeking intimacy with her, but there was no prospect of marriage. One day, she sued him in court, claiming that he always engaged in fleeting affairs during his travels. The member had no way to resist and settled by paying an enormous sum. And so it ended. Alas, Shen was truly an extraordinary figure among women. However, in the early years of the Republic, she also organized a women's Northern Expedition army, gaining considerable reputation. She was on par with Lin Zongsu in fame. Unexpectedly, she has now passed away in Shanghai. The one who once scolded like an oriole and berated like a swallow has suddenly ridden a phoenix to the paradise of immortality, never to return.

World Tidbits 129

— Hai Ke

A Large Number of Pets Owned by a Woman. Miss Beat Rice Harrigon, a famous British bass viola player, amazed and delighted the public with her singing nightingales. Most interestingly, she kept a large number of pets at home. She had all kinds of birds and beasts. She had twenty-four dogs, two short-snouted crocodiles, one monkey, one Moor hen, five parrots, twenty-eight goldfish, two mules, twenty-five budgerigars, thirty-two pigeons, twenty-four canaries, two Australian crested doves, and several other rare and precious birds. They were all her good companions in daily life. The monkey, named Jane, could dance and had good posture. One of the parrots could sing the famous song "It's a Long Way to Tipperary." One of the dogs could also bark out tunes, which was very pleasant to hear. These many pets, under her training, all had an ear for music and loved to listen to their mistress play her bass viola.

Patriotic Zeal of Ninety-Three Eighty-Six 130

— Cheng Guo

Mr. Ma Xiangbo, a ninety-three-year-old elder, published his suggestions for overcoming difficulties on the day Liaoning and Jilin were lost. His loyal advice to our compatriots across the country was filled with tearful words and penetrating insights. Later, his letter to students, as disclosed in the newspapers, provided much guidance for the patriotic movement of young people. His moral character and writing are probably already well-known throughout the country, so there is no need for me, the reporter, to say more. However, things in the world often come in pairs. At this moment when the enemy's horses and barbarian tunes are shaking the world, the people of our country have risen up in struggle for survival amidst worry and fear. The fervor of the people's movement has led to many extraordinary deeds and strange stories that the average person may not know. I will present one such instance to show that the spirit of the people cannot be insulted. Who says there is no one in China?

Qiu Gongluanxie is from Xiangyin in Hunan. He was gifted from a young age and had a revolutionary nature. In the first year of the Republic, he was commissioned by Mr. Huang Keqiang to go to Tongzhou to declare independence. On the way, he was arrested by the water police and imprisoned for five years. In the fourteenth year of the Republic, during the wars in Jiangsu and Zhejiang, he was again instructed by Sun Yat-sen to serve as the commander-in-chief of the punitive expedition against Qi. In the sixteenth year of the Republic, before the revolutionary army arrived in Shanghai, Qiu had already recruited a civilian army and engaged in fierce battles with Bi Shucheng's troops in the Baoshan Road area for a day and a night, forcing Bi's troops to retreat. Qiu then retired after achieving his goal, with no thoughts of personal gain or reward. He usually supported himself by selling his calligraphy. If anyone requested it, he would wield his brush for them without regard to the value of the work. His calligraphy was vigorous, mature, and elegant, and those leaders of the party and government who obtained it often regarded it as a treasure. Now, with the invasion by the Japanese devils, Qiu, at the age of eighty-six, did not spare his declining years and ran around shouting, his feet never stopping. He organized the Retired Soldiers Anti-Japanese National Salvation Volunteer Army of the Republic of China, seeking to fight with blood and iron for the survival of the nation. He was elected by the people as the army commander. It is said that the headquarters is currently located at the Hunan Guildhall in Xieqiao. His subordinates number around fifty to sixty thousand, all of whom have experienced battles and served in the military for a long time. They do not need training and can immediately march to the front lines. There are also quite a few guns and bullets. It is said that after Qiu organized the volunteer army, various representatives were sent to Shanghai to discuss everything. The arrangements have now been completed, and they plan to concentrate their forces in the near future and advance to the front lines, vowing to fight to the death against the Japanese invaders. They would rather die for the country than live in humiliation. Qiu, though old, is becoming stronger and will personally go to the front lines to direct everything. Such majestic spirit and firm integrity are greatly to the glory of our country. What are the thoughts of us young people upon hearing this? (No payment accepted)

▲ Brief News: The famous novelist Wang Zhusheng recently celebrated the birth of a daughter. When his wife was first pregnant, she suffered severe abdominal pain. Fortunately, through a friend's introduction, she sought the medical care of Dr. Fang Shenhe, a renowned acupuncturist from Hele Lane on Xinzha Road. With his devoted acupuncture treatment, the pregnancy was stabilized and the illness cured. It is said that Dr. Fang has cured countless dangerous and serious illnesses. For example, consumption and dropsy are among the most serious and difficult diseases to treat. Among the most dangerous situations is when pregnant women contract severe illnesses. Because it is necessary to treat the illness while protecting the fetus, Dr. Fang once used acupuncture on a pregnant woman named Dai who was seven months pregnant and suffering from appendicitis. She was experiencing excruciating abdominal pain. Dr. Fang first performed surgery to move the fetus, and then applied acupuncture to specific points to stop the pain. He then carefully repositioned the fetus to its original location. Soon after, the illness was cured, and she safely gave birth to a son. Those who heard about this were amazed by his divine skills.
