Random Musings from the Di Xiang Studio 131

— Gan Yi

Wang Naizheng

At the beginning of the Republic, Yuan Shikai transformed from a key minister of the Qing Dynasty into the head of state. For a time, many upright and virtuous officials of the previous dynasty, one after another, demeaned themselves by serving in the new court, too numerous to count after Xu Shichang. One could hardly find anyone who refused to eat the millet and beans of the new government. However, Wang Naizheng was worthy of praise for preserving his integrity and setting a good example. Naizheng, courtesy name Ping San, later styled himself as Bing Shan (Sick Mountain). He was from Zhongjiang in Sichuan. After passing the imperial examination and entering the Hanlin Academy, he became a supervising censor. His forthright criticism was renowned throughout the country. In those days, few of the noble officials who were impeached by him were not shocked. During the late Qing Dynasty, the censors mostly engaged in perfunctory tasks, using official banquets and drinking to discuss matters. They would often pick up on trivial matters and write about them in their memorials, indulging in momentary satisfaction. Those who were impeached would all use their connections to turn major matters into minor ones and minor ones into nothing at all. Naizheng, however, was different. He would not bring up matters unless they were truly substantial, nor would he impeach people unless they were truly corrupt. Therefore, people feared him. Later, the sensational exposé by the "Three Lin Company" was not without borrowing from Naizheng's tactics. The "Three Lin" were Jiang Chunlin from Fujian, Zhao Qilin from Sichuan, and Zhao Binglin from Hunan. Lin and Lin are homophones, hence the name "Three Lin Company." Since Naizheng was known for his bold speaking, the people in the Grand Council especially disliked him. Yikuang once said to someone, "Ping San makes things difficult for us in every matter. When the opportunity arises, we must send him to an outside post to avoid trouble." Therefore, he was appointed as the prefect of Fuzhou Prefecture in Jiangxi. During his three years in office, he did not take a single penny. As a result, he was widely praised. Although local officials repeatedly recommended him for his talent, he only received commendations that were recorded but not substantially used. When Puyi ascended the throne at a young age, Zaifeng served as the regent on behalf of his young son. He immediately promoted Naizheng to be the intendant of the Changzhen Circuit in Hunan, then the Surveillance Commissioner of Jiangxi. He did not take office there, but was instead appointed as the Prefect of Shuntian Prefecture. Soon after assuming office, he was transferred to be the Financial Commissioner of Henan and then to Hubei. At that time, the governor of Hubei, Chen Kuilong, was transferred to Beiyang, and the successor governor, Rui Cheng, was still serving as the governor of Jiangsu. An official order appointed Naizheng to concurrently manage the affairs of the Governor-General of Huguang, while simultaneously holding the office of prefect. This all happened in less than a year. The speed of his promotion was unparalleled in the late Qing Dynasty. This was because Naizheng had once tutored Zaifeng. Zaifeng had always known of his virtue. Once he took power, he promoted him five ranks in one year. The repayment of his patronage could be said to have been complete. After Rui Cheng arrived in Hubei, Naizheng returned to his position as financial commissioner. Because Cheng was arrogant and unaccommodating, they could not get along. Zaifeng heard about this and planned to bring him into the central government. Someone stopped him. Therefore, he was transferred to Guizhou. The path was remote and the position was barren. At first, it was thought that Naizheng might not want to go. However, he received confirmation that he was already on his way. This further confirmed that he was not a person who chose the most lucrative opportunities. If the Qing dynasty had lasted longer, Naizheng would surely have become a prime minister. However, the third year of Xuantong marked the end of the dynasty. Returning from the border, he passed through Shanghai by land and settled there. He was very poor and called himself the Qian Dao Ren (Reclusive Taoist). He became a doctor, living in seclusion. In recent years, he has grown even older and his circumstances have become even more difficult. However, he remains steadfast in upholding his integrity as before. Comparing him to the ancients, he is like Wang Wan.

The Record of the Twin Towers of Military Affairs (11) 132

— Master of the Seeking Happiness Studio

Chapter Two: Jesting with Her Good Tutor, A Terrible Report Arrives; Her Home Meets Disaster, Pitying a Friend in Solitude; A Spring Atmosphere Comes to Life in the Inn.

It turned out that her boudoir was arranged in a row of north-facing upper rooms, totaling three large rooms. The easternmost room was her bedroom, which ordinary people could not casually enter. The middle room served as a small guest room. Any guests who could be invited to the upper room had to first step into this room. The westernmost room was her study. It was decorated with extreme elegance. The walls were hung with calligraphy and paintings by famous people. A rosewood desk was placed by the window, with exquisite stationery on top. Next to it was a row of glass bookcases, sparsely filled with thread-bound books in cloth cases and Western-style books with gilded leather covers. The chairs, couches, and tea tables were all Western-style furniture made of rosewood. There were also a few antique items displayed, giving the room a refined feel. After entering the study, she went directly to a swivel chair in front of the desk and sat down. Her petite body seemed too tired to sit upright, shrinking into a ball and sinking deeply into the chair. Then, she casually pointed to another chair beside her and smiled unnaturally, saying, "Please sit, teacher. It's time for the lesson." Wei Zhuomou responded with a couple of "Yes, yes" sounds, busying himself by first finding the English textbook that she read daily from the desk. He opened it and found the page that was supposed to be continued, carefully placing it in front of her. Then, he also opened the Western-style book he had brought and placed it in front of him, before sitting down next to her. He pointed at the book and taught her to read, sentence by sentence. Unexpectedly, she was listless and acted strangely. Her eyes, which were usually lively, did not look at the book, nor did they look at the teacher's walrus mustache. Instead, they seemed like a pair of gemstones that had lost their luster, embedded in her eye sockets, as if she was staring blankly at something or lost in thought. It was so quiet that there was not a single sound. He could not see her lips moving as she followed the teacher's mumbling recitation. Wei Zhuomou, seeing that her expression was not right and unwilling to waste his effort, smiled and said, "What did I say? I said you weren't in the mood today, so we shouldn't have the lesson. But you insisted. Isn't it a waste now? You can't even read half a sentence." Liang Xiaoyun, after being said by Wei Zhuomou, also felt bored. She casually swept her hand across the book, making a "thud" sound as she knocked it off the desk and onto the carpet at her feet. She blinked her eyes, pursed her lips, and said in a spoiled tone, "I certainly wasn't in the mood to read. But you also don't seem to be willing to patiently teach me. Let's just forget it." Wei Zhuomou quickly bent down to pick it up for her, and still said with a smile, "Young lady, don't get angry. It's all my fault as the teacher. I don't know how to coax my student to read. Now it's too late to think of a way to coax you. Let's just forget it. Let's chat about something else. Or, I'll tell you a story or a joke to cheer you up." Liang Xiaoyun suddenly turned her face away and said, "I don't want to hear anything."

Financial Gold Price Decline Intensifies 133

▲ The plunge of more than eleven taels is dramatic. The gold price fell more severely yesterday, the waves were raging and unstoppable. People were unusually frightened, and finally the price dropped sharply by more than eleven taels. Securities and Bonds Still Suspended 137

▲ No Transactions Yesterday or the Day Before

▲ Market Closure Likely to Continue Today

For the past two days, Wednesday and Thursday, the Chinese Merchants Securities Exchange and brokers, concerned that the overall situation would cause prices to continue to fall, decided to only settle transactions, and then decided to suspend all transactions. Therefore, there were no transactions in those two days. The exchange held an emergency meeting the night before last to discuss solutions, deciding to await orders from the Ministry of Finance before reopening. However, brokers, seeing little chance of improvement in the current situation, convened a meeting yesterday morning and decided to extend the market closure for another two days, hoping for a better overall situation. As a result, the market remained closed yesterday, and it is feared that trading will still be difficult today. The situation will be observed again at the beginning of next week, and a decision will be made on whether to resume trading based on the intentions of the Ministry of Finance and the financial industry. The market outlook is not optimistic. All parties are levying taxes, and the Ministry of Finance is suspending payment of principal and interest on bonds. Although the news still needs to be confirmed, public anxiety has reached its peak. The banking industry, with its close ties, is deeply anxious, and other industries are also seeking support, hoping that the government will consider the difficulties of businesses, properly plan relief measures, and reassure the people, lest the future becomes more severe and the foundation of the nation is shaken.

North and South Rice Markets Stabilize 141

▲ Sources in Southern Shanghai yesterday exceeded twenty, and rural and urban transactions became active. Due to unfavorable weather and weakened confidence, thick japonica rice prices temporarily remained at the opening levels. Arrivals of early and late rice were limited, and the appetite remained thin. Street sales were brisk, with prices rising slightly. Yanglu tip rice showed signs of fatigue, presenting a weakening trend. Wine appetite was strong, and prices rose nearly a dime.

▲ Yesterday was the day for the Rice Industry Association in the City Temple of Xinzha to measure the capacity of rice measures, so transactions were not very active. Top-grade thick japonica rice prices remained the same as the previous market, with secondary grades rising nearly a dime. Some hoarders of early and late rice slightly increased their holdings, by about 2,000 piculs, and prices jumped by two or three dimes. Du tip rice showed signs of fatigue, with no price increases or decreases. Glutinous rice appetite was weak and the situation was tired. Rice merchants in the Hexia area had about 4,600 piculs in stock.

Flour Market Without Major Changes 143

▲ Many Parties Preparing for the New Year

Yesterday, the flour market was generally stable. Long positions were preparing for the New Year and had no intention of making changes. Although short positions intended to sell, there were very few buyers, making it difficult to sell smoothly. It was heard that a certain factory had ordered another ship of Australian wheat at 3.65 taels. There were also rumors that anti-Japanese efforts had become lax, and many Japanese merchants were active. It is necessary for flour factories to show conscience to avoid being criticized for their lack of patriotism. As a result, this month was down 0.0025 taels compared to the previous day, February was up 0.025 taels, March and April were down 0.005 taels, May was unchanged, and June was up 0.005 taels.

Local News

Wu Tiecheng Consults with Various Circles on Financial Issues 151

▲ Negotiations Result in a Satisfactory Outcome

▲ Unanimous Expression of Support for the Government

▲ Both Sides to Continue Discussions Today

Since the central government proposed suspending payment of principal and interest on public bonds, which aroused strong opposition from all sectors, the National Government has decided to withdraw the proposal and sent Shanghai Mayor Wu Tiecheng to Shanghai to explain and negotiate financial issues. Wu arrived in Shanghai from Nanjing yesterday morning. Yesterday afternoon at 3:15 PM, Wu personally consulted with representatives of the financial community at the Bankers' Association, and the meeting adjourned at 5:30 PM. The result was satisfactory, and the representatives all expressed their willingness to do their best to support the government through this financial crisis. The details are recorded as follows.

Representatives Present 152

Due to the public debt issue, various sectors have held repeated meetings in recent days. The night before last, after learning that the central government had sent Wu Tiecheng to Shanghai for consultations, they also selected seven representatives to be responsible for contacting Wu. The seven representatives were Zhang Gongquan, Li Fusun, Wang Xiaolai, Qin Runqing, Shi Liangcai, Du Yuesheng, and Zhang Xiaolin. The central government was represented by Wu Tiecheng and Cai Zengji, Director of the Municipal Finance Bureau. All attended the meeting at the Bankers' Association at 3:15 PM yesterday.

Contents of the Deliberations 153

After the meeting began, Wu Tiecheng first reported that the central government had established a Special Committee of the Central Political Council, with the number of members increased from nine to fifteen. This is a small group organization under the Central Political Council. The event of suspending payment of principal and interest on public bonds was only one of the proposals. Later, due to the spread of the news, it caused special panic in all parties. Most members of the Central Political Council also expressed opposition to this proposal, and the proposal was never established. Therefore, it is not really a problem. No matter what, the government will not resort to this measure. Please, representatives, relax. However, the central government's finances have reached a dead end. Please find ways to maintain the financial community to overcome this difficulty. Currently, the central government's military expenditures are at least 16 million yuan per month, and political expenditures are 2 million yuan, totaling 18 million yuan. On the revenue side, if the provinces do not deduct taxes, then 7 million yuan can be collected per month. The difference between income and expenditure is 11 million yuan, which should be assisted by the financial community for one month. The representatives stated that they could accept the principle of assisting the government proposed by Wu, but the amount of 11 million yuan was too large. It is now approaching the Lunar New Year and there is no guarantee. After detailed discussions between the two parties, it was decided that Wu would immediately telegraph Nanjing for further reduction. On the one hand, various public groups will convene another meeting last night to determine the exact amount that can be assisted by the government each month. After both parties have the results, we will discuss it again today. The representatives unanimously stated at the meeting that they would try to maintain the government no matter what. At the same time, Wu Tiecheng also said that finances would be completely open in the future and the people would have the right to supervise. In the future, all major central government policies will be presided over by the National Crisis Committee, which will recruit talents from all over the country, with about 80 members, and so on. The meeting adjourned at 5:30 PM.

Wu Tiecheng's Remarks 154

After the meeting, reporters inquired with Wu Tiecheng about the negotiations and other matters. Wu replied, and his remarks are recorded as follows: I (Wu referring to himself) went to Nanjing the other day to attend the Central Standing Committee meeting. Today, I came to Shanghai to consult with representatives of various public groups in the city on financial issues. The results of the talks can be said to be smooth. There have been rumors outside in recent days of panic that the government will suspend payment of principal and interest on public bonds, but although the government's finances have reached a dead end, it will ultimately not implement this proposal to cut off the lifeline of the national economy. This kind of news is only a minority proposal. The government did not pass it. Currently, in order to alleviate financial difficulties, I am consulting with representatives of various public groups to jointly maintain the overall situation. Today, I exchanged opinions with everyone and the results were very good. The representatives are also very willing to do their best to maintain the government, and the government is also very clear about the difficulties of the financial community. I just hope that everyone can help each other. Wu also responded to reporters' inquiries by saying that when I was in Nanjing, President Sun (Ke) told me (Wu referring to himself) that he would take the train to Hangzhou today (yesterday) to meet with Chiang to urge him to return to Nanjing. However, I am still unsure whether President Sun will go to Hangzhou today. He also said that the tax revenues in Guangdong have not been cut off and are still preserved in Guangdong and can be handed over to the central government. Zhang Hanqing (Xueliang) in North China has also not cut off tax revenues. I will not return to Nanjing immediately today. I plan to telegraph the results of the consultations to the central government and then consult with the representatives of various public groups in Shanghai.

Candidates for Minister of Finance 155

Regarding the selection of a successor to the Minister of Finance, the government initially considered Chen Mingshu. However, according to news from the banking community yesterday, the government quite intended to ask the financial community to recommend a successor. However, the financial community stated that they unanimously opposed Chen Mingshu as the chief financial officer. Other successor candidates are at the discretion of the government and are not to be questioned.

Chen and Ye Come to Shanghai for News 156

The government decided to send Minister of Industry Chen Gongbo and Minister of Railways Ye Gongchuo to Shanghai to explain to all sectors and negotiate financial issues. Chen Gongbo arrived in Shanghai yesterday and consulted with all parties. Representatives of Ye Gongchuo also arrived in Shanghai yesterday to conduct separate negotiations.

Wu Tiecheng Persuades Citizens 157

▲ Hoping Not to Strike, Boycott, or Suspend Studies

Member of the Central Committee Wu Tiecheng stated to reporters yesterday that at this time of national crisis, Mr. Sun Zhesheng has the determination to sacrifice and take office as the President of the Executive Yuan to deal with the national crisis. Although Mr. Jiang Wang Hu and others failed to come to Nanjing to share the difficulties, they all expressed their support for Mr. Sun, stabilized the central government. The people and the government are closely related. I hope all parties will trust the government and support the government. Recently, I have heard that Shanghai is brewing strikes, boycotts, and school suspensions to coerce the government to declare war on Japan as soon as possible and recover the lost territories of the Eastern Provinces by force. Although this expression comes from the people's sincere patriotism, at this time of serious diplomacy and financial difficulties, all parties should support the government and urge the government to give full support to deal with and overcome these difficulties and seek solutions to diplomatic and financial problems. This plan will only make the government more difficult and will seriously hit the Shanghai market. As the head of Shanghai Municipality, I bear the responsibility for public order in the city, and I have to give good advice on these attempts, hoping that all sectors will pay attention to this.

One Hundred and Twenty-Four Trade Associations Disagree with Boycott Proposal 158

▲ Chamber of Commerce Decides to Follow the Wishes of Its Members

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce previously received a request from the Shanghai University and Middle School Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association to boycott the market to urge the government to send troops to Japan. The Executive Committee decided that this matter was of great importance, and the executive and supervisory committees could express their acceptance, but they must seek the consent of the various trade associations. The reporter of the New Voice Agency learned that the deadline for the inquiry letter was the 15th. He went to the secretariat of the association at 6 PM last night to inquire about the results. According to the reply, the association had received formal letters from the banking industry, money industry, bean and rice industry, miscellaneous grain oil cake industry, department store industry, knitting industry, miscellaneous grain oil cake exchange, rice grain industry, Chinese and Western woodenware industry, seafood and grocery industry, burst industry, silk satin industry, candle industry, Western-style woodenware industry, sauce and liquor industry, rental car industry, new drug industry, northern goods industry, longan industry, electrical industry, ice-fresh fish industry, Shaoxing wine industry, southern goods industry, fur industry, fresh pork industry, cake silk industry, shoe industry, Sanyou Industrial Co., Ltd., silk edge industry, military uniform industry, sausage industry, sugar industry, embroidery industry, watch industry, Chinese candle industry, tea industry, bookbinding industry, color printing industry, copper and iron machinery industry, clothing industry, porcelain industry, straw hat industry, ivory ware industry, silverware industry, native cloth industry, cotton cloth industry, foil industry, jewelry industry, Chinese soap industry, paper industry, coal industry, fur and bone oil industry, Western paint industry, rice store industry, Fenjiu industry, glasses industry, bamboo industry, firewood and charcoal industry, motor silk weaving factory industry, paint woodenware industry, north and south goods dismantling industry, copper and tin industry, fresh meat industry, silk factory industry, shipping industry, etc., a total of 124 trade associations, public officials, and store members. They could not agree to a boycott. The association held its 23rd Executive Committee meeting yesterday afternoon and decided to follow the wishes of its members.

Various Road Business Federation Expresses Solemnity on Boycott 159

The Shanghai Various Road Business Federation issued a notice to all stores in the city yesterday opposing the boycott, saying that since the fall of Jinzhou, the Japanese army has been approaching Shanhaiguan, and the shocking news has spread, causing public anger to boil, and no one is not the enemy with the same hatred. Our Shanghai students, motivated by righteousness, demanded that all stores in the city boycott the market to urge the government to send troops to resist Japan and recover the lost land. The patriotic enthusiasm is admirable. Since the Wanbaoshan incident, merchants have resolutely severed economic ties with Japan and voluntarily organized the National Salvation Volunteer Army, all to fulfill their duties of saving the country. Our country has suffered countless financial damages from years of internal strife. The central government's financial income comes from the people's blood and sweat. The general stores, although glorious and spectacular in the market, support their inside with the concept of unsuredness. The life of merchants has reached such a point and it is very difficult. Especially at this time of being approached by the violent sun and the government unable to cope with it, it is also the leaders of the Central Government, Wang, Hu, Jiang, etc., who have not yet come to Beijing to preside over the central government. Even if we want to boycott the market and demand troops, I am afraid that there is nothing to respond to. If the boycott can achieve the sending of troops to recover the lost land, then what happiness would our merchants not be willing to do? At a time when the government has not decided on a major plan for national salvation, any sacrifices by the people will not help. Moreover, it is now the period for the general collection and settlement of commercial taxes. The business operations of the stores rely on this end to fund the turnover and determine profit and loss. If the market is boycotted at this time, it will inevitably cause commercial terror and financial obstruction. The final result will be of no help to the facts and will make the commercial market a chaotic state. In short, how can the merchants' patriotism be behind others? In the past, the May 30th Massacre saw a boycott of up to 27 days. Their struggle with imperialism had a great fearless revolutionary spirit. They can make saving the country practical and avoid self-inflicted troubles and unnecessary sacrifices, dare not to agree. This association is for the personal pain of the member stores and has to solemnly express its opposition to the boycott.

The General Federation of Business Circles sent a letter to the various branch associations yesterday, stating: "Recently, some people have advocated boycotting the market as the backing for diplomacy. In fact, under this situation, domestic politics has not been put on track and diplomacy has no way to proceed. Among the leaders of the Kuomintang government who claim to save the country and the people, there are different strategies among the same party, scattered in all directions, and disregarding the national crisis. Even if the market is boycotted, the gentlemen will surely regard it as nothing and consider it a good thing, and the violent sun will not be able to damage it in the slightest. After all, this kind of action is a sacrifice. Sacrifice must have a price. This association believes that the act of boycotting the market is ultimately unavoidable when necessary, but it is absolutely impossible under the current state. This association's members, in the midst of saving the country and the people, must have the determination to use the boycott as a last resort, but they absolutely cannot abuse it. This letter is to inform your association to notify all members."

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Intensifies Inspection Work 161

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce's Committee for Implementing Economic Sanctions Against Japan held its eighth standing meeting yesterday. It was resolved that (1) send a letter to the court to handle the matter strictly according to the law, (2) notify all sectors to sever ties with Dafeng, (3) send a letter to the yarn industry inspection team to report on fellow traders privately importing Japanese yarn as much as possible in order to warn unscrupulous merchants.

Ma Zhanshan's Representative Han Liru Discusses the Black Province's War Achievements 177

▲Speech at Fuchang Tobacco Company

▲Presented in a Private Capacity

General Ma Zhanshan, Chairman of Heilongjiang Province, sent his representative Han Liru to Shanghai to report the truth about Heilongjiang Province to all sectors. Yesterday afternoon at 2 p.m., Mr. Han, in a private capacity, reported on General Ma's bloody battles and recent attitudes at the Fuchang Tobacco Company. His remarks are as follows:

"Brothers, I am here in a personal capacity to discuss General Ma's battle achievements, not as a representative. First, I must describe

Ma's History 178

He is a graduate of the military academy. He became famous in the Northeast for suppressing bandits. His methods of attacking bandits were slightly different from those of ordinary soldiers, in that he would seize the opportunity to attack before the bandits were ready. He was very agile and decisive, so his fame spread far and wide. I once traveled with the general and saw that the Russian border defense was tight and the soldiers were very energetic. Because of this, he decided to build up Heilongjiang. This was before the September 18th Incident. When Zhang Haipeng betrayed the country for the Japanese, General Ma telegraphed all sectors that, no matter what, he must

Fulfill His Duty to Defend the Territory 179

and never allow an inch of territory to be lost. Now Chairman Wan (Fulin) is not in Heilongjiang Province, and we must not retreat. Later, Beiping ordered General Ma to go to the provincial capital and act as chairman. At that time, Zhang Haipeng's troops also arrived at the provincial capital from Taonan. The garrison in the city knew that Zhang Haipeng had the support of the Japanese army and dared not confront them, so they retreated. General Ma then went to take over. On the 20th, he acted as chairman, on the one hand advising Zhang Haipeng not to be a lackey of the Japanese, and on the other hand using force to resist. Zhang retreated in a roundabout way, and the Japanese, using the excuse that the construction of the Nenjiang Bridge was funded by Japanese loans and that the bridge was damaged and needed to be repaired by the Japanese, but the general said that the damage to the bridge could be repaired by our side, so he refused. Until the 31st, the Japanese army suddenly notified General Ma that Commander Honjo ordered that the bridge must be repaired. That afternoon, the Japanese army went to Dajin Station and broke through our army's front. General Ma immediately notified the Japanese consul that the Liaoning Incident was the greatest unfortunate event, and if more unfortunate events occurred, the responsibility would be borne by the Japanese side. I (Han referring to himself) and the adjutant went to negotiate with the Japanese side, but as soon as we arrived at the front line,

War Began 180

Because General Ma held a meeting on the evening of the previous day, saying that if the Japanese army came to attack and we did not resist, Heilongjiang Province would become part of Japan's territory. General Ma's soldiers also said that they would rather die under Chinese law than be trampled on by the Japanese army. At the beginning of the fire, the Japanese threw many bombs. The 31st was the first battle, and the first and second days were the period when the Japanese painstakingly used military fire. At that time, some advocated retreating to Hailun, but General Ma disagreed and was willing to fight to the death. He would retreat only after being defeated by the Japanese army. At one time, more than 10,000 people were mobilized, and the Japanese army had 6,000 to 8,000 participants. Our army then

Vigorously Attacked the Japanese寇 181

were all very brave, but the Japanese army gained the upper hand everywhere because of the sharpness of its machine guns, and secretly sent cavalry to抄 our rear, resulting in a disadvantageous retreat to Sanjianfang. From this, it can be seen that although the Japanese are said to be strong, our military strategy is not weaker than theirs, and we are quite capable of dealing with them. The Japanese military weapons are sharper than ours, but the battle is only like this. At this point, the Chinese are no longer afraid of the Japanese army. The Battle of the Nenjiang Bridge really opened a new era in the psychological warfare between the Chinese and the Japanese. If this kind of psychology can be expanded, the Chinese will definitely be able to 制先 the Japanese. The Japanese even tried to alienate our country's feelings with the international community, and made counter-propaganda to the international community, claiming that our country's ability to win was actually due to collusion with the Russians. From November 4th to 16th, there were

Military Attaches Observing 182

the inside story of our army. As a result, the Japanese side's counter-propaganda failed, and this was the period to prove that the Chinese can fight. By the 16th, 17th, 18th, 19th and other days, the Japanese side transported more tanks and ammunition. On the evening of the 19th, General Ma returned from the front line to supervise the battle. At first, he thought that the Japanese could not cross the Middle East Road, but the Japanese actually crossed the road and came over the mountains and fields. At that time, the general trend was gone, and General Ma had no choice but to retreat. However, the reasons for the retreat are as follows: ㈠ The Chinese army had no new guns and no reinforcements. ㈡ There were no planes in the Chinese army, and it can be proved that the international community cannot be relied on and must be self-determined by the people. Only Ma

General's Recent Situation 183

is still good. The nearby vanguard is under his command, partly because of Ma's prestige and partly because of patriotism. Now there is a lack of food and bullets, but fortunately, a lot of remittances from all over the country have arrived in Heilongjiang. His army has adopted guerrilla warfare.

General's Will 184

will never change, and he must strive for the country's honor and sacrifice for the nation, and vow not to coexist with the Japanese. News from this city 二

Inside Story of Japanese Cotton Mills Canceling Monthly Bonuses 196

▲ Intending to Prolong Workers' Strike

▲ Enabling Factories to Save Expenses

The workers of Japanese-owned Kiwa Cotton Mill, Nichihua Cotton Mill, and Silk Mill in the Caojiadu area of western Shanghai are staging strikes in succession because the factories canceled their monthly bonuses. Although the Municipal Government, Municipal Party Headquarters, Social Affairs Bureau, Public Security Bureau, and the Sixth District Police Department have sent personnel to mediate, and the Joint Association of Cotton Mill Workers has offered assistance, the attitude of the factory owners is firm, so there is still no hope of a resolution. It is learned that the Japanese-owned factories are implementing a uniform cancellation of the monthly bonus as a deliberate and exploitative plan. The Japanese factory owners have repeatedly held meetings and agreed to adhere to this policy. Since the September 18th Incident, the Japanese factories have suffered greatly from the boycott movement. Maintaining the status quo has been difficult. Seeing no hope of resolving the situation and facing endless losses, the Japanese factory owners discussed implementing a temporary shutdown. However, they realized that such a shutdown would create the following problems:

(1) If the factory announced a shutdown, all employees would have to be paid severance, pension, and bonuses.

(2) Most of the current workers have been employed for many years and are well-trained. If the factory were to shut down, they might be hired by Chinese-owned factories. If the factory were to reopen, it might be difficult to recruit workers.

(3) If the Japanese staff were to be laid off, they would have no income and face hardship. Therefore, the Japanese factory owners have hesitated to implement a shutdown. Unable to shut down but finding it difficult to continue operations, the Japanese factory owners have been anxious. As a last resort, after repeated discussions among all the Japanese factory owners, they decided that canceling the monthly bonus would be the only policy. By provoking the workers to revolt and stage strikes, the factory owners could refuse to compromise, thus prolonging the strike and allowing the factory to save expenses and achieve its intended purpose. Thus, the cancellation of monthly bonuses by the Japanese factories is a strategy to exploit workers and induce them to strike on their own, while the workers are being deceived.

Further Report on the Robbery of the Baofeng Steamer by Pirates 197

▲ Normal Departure Yesterday

▲ Passengers Refused

The Baofeng steamer of the Jufeng Baoji Company in Nanshi, Shanghai, was robbed on its way from Shanghai to Chongming, and one passenger was killed. This incident was reported in yesterday's newspaper. The details of the incident are reported as follows:

Robbery Situation 198

The pirates boarded the ship disguised as passengers in Shanghai. There were more than thirty of them, mixed in with the steerage passengers. The steamer departed at 8:00 PM on the 13th. At 9:30 PM, it reached Wusong, and at 9:45 PM, it arrived at the Sanxia Waterway. The pirates emerged from the cabin and fired pistols as a warning. Four bandits rushed to the bow and took the ship owner under surveillance. They ordered the first mate, Yuan Shengpin, to change course. When the first mate refused, he was beaten by the bandits. The bandits then took control of the ship themselves. Another group of bandits rushed to the engine room. The chief engineer was on leave, so the second engineer took his place. The bandits called out, "Please help us." All the positions on the ship were taken over by the pirates, and the crew members were locked in the cabins.

Looting of All Cabins 199

Four of the pirates carried pistols, while the others used knives and other weapons. After taking control of the ship, they entered the purser's office and forced Deng Chunmao to hand over money. When Deng hesitated, he was beaten by the bandits. Deng did not resist and allowed them to search the office. They looted more than 2,800 yuan in cash and more than 700 yuan of the purser's personal funds. They also took his leather coat, gold ring, and other belongings. After looting the purser's office, they entered the main cabin and searched the passengers. There were more than 500 passengers on the ship. They were searched one by one, and even those who had one yuan were robbed. Clothes and jewelry were taken as well. The passengers were robbed of more than 1,700 yuan in cash. After the robbery, the passengers were locked in the main cabin. The pirates then went to the upper deck and searched the crew members. It can be said that the pirates looted the Baofeng steamer so thoroughly that no one was left with a single penny.

Passenger Killed 200

While the pirates were looting, gunshots rang out like a string of beads. The passengers screamed for help. The Xinsheng steamer of the Xinglong Company passed by and heard the gunshots and screams from the Baofeng steamer. They knew that it was being robbed and that the Baofeng was heading towards Daxieshan. When the Xinsheng arrived at Qinglong Port, it sent a telegram to the Jufeng Company in Shanghai at 10:00 AM on the 14th. That night, when the ship was being looted, a passenger shouted for help and was shot dead by the pirates. The body was abandoned in the main cabin.

Five People Injured 201

Two passengers, Shi Jinzhang and others, were shot for resisting the pirates. The crew members who were injured by the pirates were First Mate Yuan Shengpin, Third Engineer Lin A'kai, and Tea Boy Cao Linjiang. They were all wounded by the pirates with knives. After the steamer returned to Shanghai yesterday, they were sent to Nanyang Hospital and Shanghai Hospital for treatment.

Loss of Goods 202

After taking the cash, the bandits opened the cargo hold and took away one bolt of cloth, twelve dan of soybean oil, and other miscellaneous goods, as well as clothing from passengers and crew members. At 5:30 AM on the 14th (after nine hours of looting), when the ship arrived in the waters off Daxieshan, the bandits first sounded the whistle twice, then fired a shot into the air, and then used a flashlight to signal the sea. Two large sailboats arrived, and the bandits took the stolen goods from the passenger cabins onto the sailboats and escaped to their hideout.

Boiler Dismantled 203

Before leaving, the bandits declared that because the crew members did not resist, they would not damage the ship. However, fearing that they would be pursued, they dismantled the three boilers in the ship's engine room so that it could not move. After they left, the ship owner reassembled the three boilers and then lit the fires and sailed to Shanghai, so the delay was considerable.

Examination of the Corpse 204

After the ship arrived in Shanghai, the Jufeng Company reported the incident to the Haihai Association, which in turn reported it to the court. At 4:30 PM yesterday, the court sent personnel to the ship to examine the body of the passenger who had been shot dead by the bandits. After the examination, the body was handed over to the association for safekeeping. Since there were no relatives, the body will be kept until claimed.

Hosting Distressed Passengers 205

After the passengers returned to Shanghai, all of their money had been robbed, and their luggage and clothing were gone. The Jufeng Company provided them with food and accommodation, and bought tickets for them on the Baohua and other steamers to send them back to their hometowns in Chongming and other places.

Fumigation and Disinfection of the Ship 206

Since there had been a passenger killed on the ship, according to customs regulations, the ship must be fumigated and disinfected before it can sail again. Yesterday afternoon, the ship was fumigated by the Jianghai Customs, and the fumigation was completed at 10:00 PM. Therefore, the steamer will not carry third-class passengers on its trip to Chongming, but cargo will be loaded as usual. The steamer is scheduled to depart for Chongming at 1:00 AM this morning. The robbery of the Baofeng steamer resulted in the death of one passenger, injuries to five crew members and passengers, and the loss of more than 5,000 yuan in cash, as well as a large amount of clothing and jewelry.

League of Nations Engineering Inspection Group Visits the City Center 207

The League of Nations Engineering Inspection Group, a group of five people led by Mr. Haas, Minister of Transportation of the League of Nations, arrived in China at the beginning of the month. The members of the group include Mr. Berriais, Mr. Godd, Dr. Civic, and Mr. Budley. Mr. Berriais is the chief engineer of the Paris City Road and Bridge Management Office and the secretary of the Road and Bridge Committee. He has served as the chief engineer in Annam, Tokyo, and other places. The flood control plan for Tokyo was planned by Mr. Berriais, who is a world-renowned flood control expert. Mr. Godd is the founder of the famous British engineering company "Goddway Engineering Company" and is currently a member of the British Engineering Society. He has extensive experience in harbors and all river engineering. Mr. Civic is currently the director of the Hamburg Harbor Management Office in Germany and is also a water conservancy expert. Mr. Budley has been involved in flood control projects in Java, Sumatra, and other places for many years. The above individuals are all well-known figures in the engineering field. The purpose of their visit to China is to inspect the engineering situation in China and study engineering improvement issues. The city center area plan is one of China's great new construction projects. At 9:00 AM on the 14th, the group was accompanied by Mr. Shen, Director of the Municipal Engineering Bureau, to visit Wusong and the city center area. In the afternoon, they went to Pudong to conduct an on-site inspection. It is rumored that the issue of improving the Shanghai port will be discussed.

Wenmiao Park Library to Open Soon 208

Wenmiao Park, which was built after the completion of the reconstruction of Wenmiao Road in Ximen, was informally opened to the public on the 1st and 2nd of this month. Nearly 10,000 people visited the park during the two days. However, due to minor construction projects in the park and the construction of the former Minglun Primary School on the site, which is being prepared for an exhibition room of the Public Education Center, the park gates are still closed as usual. There is a library in the park, which is an oriental-style building that showcases brilliance to the fullest extent. However, the library is deep and the light is not very adequate. The director of the library has recently been appointed by the Municipal Education Bureau as Zhuang Yun. Zhuang once held an important position at the Palace Museum in Beiping. The layout of the library is mostly complete. The books purchased are currently being processed. In addition, major bookstores in Shanghai have donated approximately 3,000 volumes of books to the library. The office of the Municipal Public Education Center is located in the Chong Sheng Temple. Since the new year, the center has been operating in accordance with the organizational regulations set by the Municipal Education Bureau, dividing into general affairs, editing, and lecturing sections. The director of the center, Li Dachao, took office yesterday. It is rumored that the opening of Wenmiao Park and the library is scheduled for the 25th of this month. The park will be open to the public for sightseeing. From then on, Shanghai will have a new recreational garden for public education. Because the park is located in a convenient transportation area in the city center, it is expected that there will be many visitors during the spring and autumn.

Wu Laiji Shipping Company Smuggles Japanese Coal 209

▲ Bargemen's Guild Resolves Severe Punishment

The Shanghai Coal and Stone Bargemen's Guild held an emergency meeting at 3:00 PM yesterday, with Ruan Xuetao as chairman. The chairman began by reporting on a letter from the Coal Industry Association. The letter stated that Yongchang had privately purchased Japanese coal, and that the bargeman was Wu Jingen, a member of the guild. At a time when Japan is rampant and the country is in a state of indignation, such an unfortunate incident has occurred, which is regrettable. Moreover, Wu Jingen is a Japanese goods inspector of the guild, stationed at the Xin Sanjing Coal Stack. Knowing the situation, he knowingly violated the rules. It was proposed how should he be punished and a unanimous resolution was made:

(1) His membership will be revoked and he will not be allowed to enter the market.

(2) A letter will be sent to the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association to actively handle the matter.

(3) A letter will be sent to the Coal Industry Association and the Sand and Gravel Industry Association, informing all coal and sand and gravel businesses that they should refuse to let him transport goods in the future.

(4) If any member of the guild colludes with Wu Jingen to act as a substitute, they will be dealt with in accordance with the previous resolution.

Guo Biao's Nephew Stabbed by Friend in Cangzhou 210

▲ Quarrel Arising from Debt Collection

▲ Also Involving a Woman

Guo Hanqing, the nephew of the late merchant Guo Biao, has many friends. He has been running a long-term room at 301 Cangzhou Hotel on Jing'an Temple Road for a year. At about 12:30 AM yesterday morning, his friend Qiu Mengrong visited Guo at Cangzhou. The two suddenly quarreled. Qiu took out a small knife and stabbed Guo Hanqing in the chest, causing serious injuries. The Jing'an Temple Police Department sent detectives to arrest Qiu and sent the injured person to the hospital for treatment. It is said that Guo and Qiu have known each other for a long time and have a close relationship. They not only enjoy each other's company but also share their wealth. Before the incident yesterday morning, Qiu came in from the outside and first talked to Guo on the phone. Guo then went downstairs to the lobby in front of the accounting room. After the two met, Qiu seemed to be collecting a debt from Guo. However, harsh words were exchanged, and Guo was stabbed by Qiu with a small knife. It is also said that Guo owed Qiu about 600 yuan. In addition, a woman was involved, inevitably causing jealousy and leading to this misfortune. Qiu Mengrong, who was arrested by the police, is the son of a landlord in the Xinminjie area of Jing'an Temple Road, but he has long held Portuguese citizenship. Guo Hanqing is currently being treated at Baolong Hospital. The knife wound is below the ribs and breast. If the injury worsens, it is a serious matter.

Huang Baiying and Tong Sanmao to Meet Again in Court 211

▲ Tong Sanmao Appeals to the Third Instance

▲ Supreme Court Sends Case Back for Retrial

In the spring of the 19th year of the Republic, Huang Baiying, a dancer, formed an unbreakable bond with Tong Sanmao, the young owner of Renkang Hardware Store at 316 East Broadway, at the Datong Dance Hall. From then on, they danced together every night, showing great affection. At dawn on June 29th of that year, Tong took her from the Paris Dance Hall in a car to the seaside in Wusong, intending to commit suicide by drowning. However, they changed their minds. On the way back to Shanghai, Tong got out of the car, bought poison, and went to the Cangzhou Hotel, intending to commit suicide together. When Huang Baiying swallowed the poison first, Tong suddenly did not want to die. The police were informed and immediately sent detectives to take Huang Baiying to the hospital. Fortunately, she was rescued quickly. Tong was charged with abetting suicide and prosecuted in the Provisional Court. After the trial, the evidence was conclusive, and he was sentenced to two years in prison. Tong did not accept the verdict and appealed, but the result was still the same. Since then, Tong has been imprisoned in the West Prison of Tilanqiao. Huang Baiying's fame has spread far and wide, and dance halls and singers are vying to hire her. She has now abandoned her dancing career and become a famous actress. Tong Sanmao has been in prison for nearly a year and a half, and no one has visited him. However, he still does not accept the crime he was convicted of. Therefore, after losing the second instance, he immediately appealed to the third instance. The Supreme Court in Nanjing reviewed the case files of the two instances in detail and finally ruled that the case should be sent back for retrial. The Second Branch of the Jiangsu Higher Court, which heard the second instance, has received the order from the Supreme Court and has scheduled a retrial for the afternoon of February 22nd. The presiding judge, Song Yuan, has issued summonses to all the witnesses and notified the police, the prosecuting attorney Li Zhishan, and the attorneys representing Tong and Huang to appear in court for arguments. It is expected that there will be many spectators on that day.

Car Horn Scares Horse, Causing Major Disaster 212

▲ Three People Injured, One Dead

Chen Deqian, a garbage cart driver from Yancheng who worked for the Public Works Department of the Municipal Council, was driving a No. 5 horse-drawn cart on the afternoon of the 13th of this month at 1:20 PM, passing near Beisichuan Road and Road. The traffic light was red at that location, so he could not proceed and stopped the cart to wait. A certain car suddenly sounded its horn, and the sound was very loud. The horse was startled and jumped violently, breaking the leather straps and running north on Hainan Road towards Tiantong Road. The driver Chen was unable to restrain the horse, which knocked down Du Qinfu, a cyclist from Songjiang, Jin Qingrong, a rickshaw puller from Jiangbei, and Wang Youcai, a twenty-one-year-old rickshaw puller (from Jiangbei), all of whom were injured. West Indian detectives from the Hongkou Police Station, including Hua Detective An Sibeng, arrived at the scene after hearing the news. The three injured persons were taken to Tongren Hospital for treatment. A Western ticket seller on a public bus saw the incident and bravely stepped forward to stop the horse, realizing that it was a No. 5 garbage cart from the Public Works Department that had caused the accident. After a while, the driver Chen Deqian arrived and turned himself in to the police. One of the injured, Wang Youcai, was fatally injured and died in the hospital in the evening. The body was sent to the Philo Road autopsy station. The First Special District Court sent a prosecutor to the station to confirm the death and make arrangements for the coffin. Yesterday morning, the police sent Chen Deqian to the First Court. The police attorney, Zhang Tianyin, presented the case and stated that the family members of the deceased, Wang Youcai, were all in their hometown. Today, the injured Du and Jin were present in court. He also presented the broken leather strap for inspection. The Chinese and Western detectives and the ticket seller also testified about the situation at the time. Du Qinfu testified that he was a messenger for a company at No. 2 Hong Kong Road and was fortunate to have suffered only minor injuries and had already recovered. The rickshaw puller Jin Qingrong suffered a severe injury to his right leg and had to be carried in and seated on the ground. He was unable to stand and briefly described the circumstances of the injury. The court ordered a medical examination to assess the injuries. The driver Chen Deqian confessed that the horse jumped violently when it heard the car horn, breaking the leather straps, and he was unable to restrain it, causing the accident. He asked the court to consider this. Judge Shen Bingrong, after , ordered that he be remanded in custody pending sentencing.

Infant's Head Severed in Gruesome Incident 213

▲ Cruel Actions Related to Flower Gambling

A two-foot-long red-painted thin-board coffin was abandoned on the side of Maishiai Road in the French Concession Shilou Road the night before. At around 10:00 AM yesterday, the coffin was discovered, and the lid was pried open, revealing the body of an infant inside. The infant's head had been severed, causing great alarm. Passersby reported the incident to the French Concession Police Station, who dispatched detectives to investigate. It was determined that the body in the coffin was that of a female infant, five or six months old. No family members were found. The body and the coffin were taken to the Tongren Fuyuan Branch Autopsy Station. According to the detective's investigation, a rickshaw puller in the area said that he had seen the coffin abandoned on the side of the road the night before. The coffin lid was intact. This morning, he saw that the coffin was covered with a straw mat, and the coffin lid had been pried open. The detective reported the information to the police chief, who ordered that the court be notified today to send personnel to conduct an autopsy and determine the cause of death. It is speculated that the infant's head was severed by flower gambling gamblers to pray for dreams in order to win the flower gambling. Otherwise, why would a five- or six-month-old infant have any grievances with anyone, and why would they be subjected to such cruelty after death?

Shen Chengfu Case Rescheduled for Further Hearing 214

Shen Chengfu, a compradore for the British-owned Tahe Foreign Firm, absconded with a large sum of money. He was later apprehended by the police, and the firm filed a criminal lawsuit against him, alleging that he had embezzled 3.5 million yuan. The First Special District Court ordered the defendant to post bail of 200,000 yuan pending trial. Yesterday was the date for the continued hearing. The defendant's attorney requested a rescheduling, stating that the defendant had recently fallen ill and was unable to personally review the accounts at the plaintiff's firm. However, the plaintiff's attorney, Lu Xingyuan, opposed the postponement. After a lengthy debate with the defendant's attorney, Jiang Yiping, the judge Xu ruled in court that the rescheduling would be permitted.

Jiangshun Steamer Troublemakers 215

There are often troublemakers on the Yangtze River steamers traveling between Shanghai and Hankou. On this occasion, on the 14th of this month, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Jiangshun Steamer returned to Shanghai from Hankou. When the ship reached the Jiujiang area, more than a dozen ruffians led by Tian Zhiquan forcibly boarded the ship, making a living by gambling and swindling money. After boarding the ship, they forcibly took food, and crew members and sailors were often beaten. When the Jiangshun Steamer arrived at Liuhe, the ruffian Tian Zhiquan impersonated a ticketing officer and extorted fares from passenger Wang Rufang. Wang Rufang refused to pay because he was not a ticketing officer. Tian Zhiquan became angry and, together with his accomplices, beat Wang Rufang, causing him to bleed profusely and nearly killing him. Seeing that they had caused a life-threatening injury, Tian and his group threw Wang Rufang into the river, intending to cover up the crime. Fortunately, passenger Wei Zhengtang saw the incident and reported it to the ticketing officer, who notified the escorting military police. The military police apprehended the assailant Tian Zhiquan and the witness Wei Zhengtang. Yesterday, when the Jiangshun Steamer arrived in Shanghai, the assailant and the witness Wei Zhengtang were sent to the Songhu Garrison Headquarters for investigation.

Zhuang Bosheng Dies in Anger at Japanese 217

▲ Suicide Note Urges Awareness from Authorities

Zhuang Bosheng, a local oiler at the Japanese-owned Tongxing Cotton Mill, lived in the countryside on Binlang Road. He participated in the workers' petition the other day after being forced to retire by the Japanese. On his way home, he passed by Robert Sheng Road and could not help but glare at a small squad of Japanese soldiers nearby. The Japanese soldiers grabbed him and beat him without asking any questions. By the time the patrolling police arrived, the Japanese soldiers had already fled. In anger, Zhuang went home and told people that the people of weak countries were not even worth as much as dogs and horses. He then closed the door and went to bed. He wrote a suicide note, which said that a great man in this world could not have great vision. Rather than living a humble life, it would be better to die to awaken the authorities. He did not care whether it was right or wrong. After writing the note, he drank all the sedative he had bought for insomnia in the past. When his family saw that Zhuang had not woken up yesterday morning, his wife suspected that he was ill and asked him. She found that he had no breath and felt icy cold. She began to cry loudly. His family found an empty bottle and a suicide note next to his pillow. His brother reported the incident to the workers at the factory, who will keep the note as a memento.

The Problem of Transporting Huge Quantities of US Relief Wheat 221

▲ Telegram from Yu Hede to Song Ziwen

Regarding the matter of foreign merchants transporting relief wheat, Director Yu of the Relief Flood Disaster Association's Transportation Group has sent two telegrams to Chairman Song, but has not yet received a reply. The text of the telegrams is as follows: (1) "To Minister Song in Nanjing, re: Relief wheat for the flood disaster, bids were invited for transportation. At yesterday's meeting, foreign merchants bid a rate of 3.25 silver cents per bag for wooden barges and 5.25 silver cents for iron barges, plus a handling fee of 1 silver cent per bag. Chinese merchants bid 3.7 silver cents for wooden barges, equivalent to 2.68 yuan, which is 0.57 silver cents cheaper per bag than the foreign merchants, and there is no handling fee. I suggest contracting with Chinese merchants to save expenses. Please approve and instruct. Yu Hede." (2) "To Minister Song of the Ministry of Finance in Nanjing, re: Transporting relief wheat for the Flood Relief Association, a telegram was previously sent. It was expected that you would investigate and handle the matter. Currently, the relief wheat is still being transported by the foreign merchant Brownell & Co. They are using large iron barges, the holds of which are hard and the bottom is deep. When loading, the bags are dropped from a height. When loading onto ships, they are hooked up, resulting in many broken bags. Furthermore, each barge carries at least 200 tons, causing delays and losses during loading and unloading. These problems can be avoided by using wooden barges. It is also heard that a significant amount of wheat has leaked from the bottom of the foreign merchant's iron barges, which they refuse to sweep up and load onto the ships. The loss in weight will be considerable. As the person in charge of transportation, I am deeply aware of the advantages and disadvantages. Furthermore, as this matter concerns disaster relief and is the focus of public attention, I must report it in advance to clarify my responsibility. I beg you to consider and approve my previous telegram to switch to Chinese merchants using wooden barges to facilitate transportation and reduce losses. Your instructions will be greatly appreciated. Yu Hede."

Closing Ceremony 224

At 2:00 PM, the inauguration of the executive and supervisory committee members and the closing ceremony continued at the original location. Guests included Gong Yuting and Li Menglan, representatives from the Shanghai Federation of Trade Unions, Yu Xianglin, Li Wenzhen, and Wang Weisheng from the Directorate General of Posts, and Lin Zhuowu, a representative from the Shanghai Postal Workers' Union. The attendees included the representatives from the congress, the presidium, and the recorders as before. First, Chairman Yu Qixiang delivered a speech (the speech is recorded below). Then, the oath-taking ceremony for the executive and supervisory committee members was held. Gu Zhengxun (Hebei), a representative elected by the congress, delivered a speech of encouragement. Executive Committee Member Huang Gongfu and Supervisory Committee Member Lao Jieming delivered acceptance speeches. Then, Li Mengkai, a representative from the Shanghai Federation of Trade Unions, delivered a speech (the speeches are omitted). Next, representatives Zheng Yipeng, Hu Man, Gu Gongfu, Liang Shaoshu, Kang Yong, and Wang Shiying delivered speeches in succession. The ceremony then concluded successfully.

Closing Address 225

Closing speech by Yu Qixiang, Chairman of the Congress: "Distinguished guests, fellow representatives, I, as the chairman of this congress, would like to deliver this address. As we speak different dialects, I would like to ask Comrade Lao Jieming to translate. This representative congress has been in preparation for several years before finally being able to convene in Shanghai today. Representatives from sixteen regions have attended, and the discussion of proposals over the past few days has been very smooth. Therefore, I believe that the future is very promising. As to why this congress took so many years to achieve, the reason is that culture has not yet been popularized and politics has not yet been put on the right track. Since we know that we cannot compare with Europe and America in terms of culture and technology, we should work harder to catch up. The postal service has a great relationship with various aspects of society. We, who serve the postal service, have a particularly close relationship with all sectors of society because scholars, farmers, workers, and merchants all need the postal service to provide indirect assistance. Therefore, we who serve should cherish the postal service. This is fulfilling our duty to all sectors of society. Therefore, the postal service is the crystallization of our employees' efforts. Since this crystallization has such a great relationship with society, we should do our best to support and develop it. If it were in a politically enlightened country, the postal service would not need its employees to exert themselves to seek development, but China is not such a country. Therefore, we should pay extra attention to ensuring that it gets fully developed. However, we postal employees should always do our best, and not shrink back because we feel that the current environment is bad. This time, there have been many good proposals, which have been jointly discussed by representatives from various regions for several days. Now they have all been handed over to the executive committee to implement, so that they can be realized in due course. At the same time, I hope that we postal workers will act according to principles, so that the resolutions can be successfully completed as soon as possible."

Groundbreaking Ceremony for the Third Dry Dock at the Jiangnan Shipyard Yesterday 226

▲ Can Accommodate Warships of 20,000 Tons or More

▲ Estimated Cost of 2 Million Yuan, Completion by the End of the Year

丨Simultaneous Keel-Laying Ceremony for Two New Naval Gunboats丨

Since assuming control of the Navy, Navy Chief Chen Shaokuan has spared no effort in construction. His first plan was to order the Jiangnan Shipyard to build the third dry dock for military use. The groundbreaking ceremony was held at the Gaochang Temple Shipyard at 10:00 AM yesterday. After the ceremony, the keel-laying ceremony was held for the new gunboats Hai Ning and Jiang Ning. Details are as follows:

Dry Dock Groundbreaking 227

The third dry dock is located on the west side of the shipyard, on land exchanged with the arsenal, totaling more than ten acres. At 11:00 AM, Chen Shaokuan used a shovel to break ground on the soil surrounded by white powder. Then, Chief Engineer Mai Gen and the heads of various departments followed suit, shoveling the soil within the enclosure, completing the ceremony.

Attendees 228

Attendees at yesterday's ceremony included Chen Jiliang, Vice Minister of Naval Affairs and Commander of the First Fleet, Zheng Gongyao, captain of the Minsheng warship, Chen Yongqin, captain of the Ding'an warship, Jia Qin, captain of the Tongji warship, Xie Weiliang, captain of the Jiao Ri warship, Zhang Rizhang, captain of the Xian Ning warship, Zhang Tianxiang, deputy captain of the Pu'an warship, Ye Baoqi, commander of the naval guard battalion, and dozens of other important officials from the Jiangnan Shipyard.

Project Overview 229

The new dry dock being built is the largest in the country, measuring 600 feet long, 65 feet wide, and 22 feet deep. If funding is sufficient, it can be completed by the end of this year. The estimated cost is over 2 million yuan. It can accommodate warships of 20,000 tons or more.

Keel Laying 230

After the groundbreaking ceremony for the third dry dock, the keel-laying ceremony for the two new naval gunboats was held at the shipyard. Ye Zaifu, head of the shipbuilding department, laid the first rivet. The two ships are coastal patrol gunboats, each costing approximately 100,000 yuan. They are expected to be completed in one year. After completion, they will be dispatched to the coastal areas to suppress bandits, as the Navy believes that the existing warships are insufficient to patrol the coast and rivers where bandits appear frequently.

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to various trade associations yesterday stating that it had received a letter from the Shanghai Municipal Finance Bureau's Business Tax Collection Office, which stated that it had received an order from the Finance Bureau to extend the deadline for filing business tax returns for various industries in the city for January 21 to January 22, in accordance with Article 11 of the Collection Regulations, to facilitate the process. The Municipal Government instructed that the extension of one year, as requested in the report, was too long. This is to be followed accordingly. This letter is to be forwarded to the various industries for their information and compliance.

Three-Year-Old Child Burned to Death 235

Jiang Shiming, a resident of Cangyang Road, Hubu, in Shanghai's East District, earns a living pushing a cart outside. His wife, Ni, went out to do odd jobs, leaving their young son, Xinglong (three years old), at home. Because it was cold, they placed him in a straw stack with a brazier at the bottom for warmth. The charcoal fire in the brazier was too intense and ignited the straw. The child cried out in pain, but there was no one to help him. Soon, he was burned to death. When Jiang Shiming returned home in the afternoon, he smelled smoke. He entered the room and saw that his son's body was charred and lifeless in the straw stack. It was a tragic sight.

Reason for Stockout at Huada Pharmacy 244

▲ A Large Shipment Has Now Arrived

The Lion Brand beef juice and chicken juice, made with cold-pressed salt by the German Malta Pharmaceutical Factory, managed by this port’s Huada Pharmacy, has seen a surge in sales in the past year. During this time when gift-giving is prevalent, the pharmacy was unable to meet market demand and was extremely apologetic. A large shipment of beef juice and chicken juice has now arrived, so those who wish to purchase the products will not have to make a wasted trip.

Later, it was learned that the child still had a biological mother, Zhang Liu, at home. A letter was sent to her asking her to come to Shanghai to claim him, and a letter was sent to Li Xuemo, the magistrate of Wuqiao County Government, asking him to summon Zhanghua locally to obtain a concrete guarantee before coming to claim him. Zhang Liu arrived in Shanghai the other day, going straight to the Children's Education and Care Center to meet Zhang Changsheng. After speaking, they embraced and cried bitterly. She was grateful that the Children's Welfare Association was able to speak out for justice and seek happiness for abused children. With his great-uncle Zhang Liechen as a witness and Tongxingheji as a guarantor, a guarantee was given to the Children's Welfare Association. The association has handed over Zhang Changsheng to his biological mother, and the family has been reunited.

Letters to the Editor 250

To the Editor: I read in the local news section of your newspaper on the 14th of this month that the Pubin Bank in Minhang Town, the first district of your county, was robbed of 4,000 yuan. However, there is no Pubin Bank in Minhang Town. The only financial institution is our Puhai Bank, and there has been no robbery. We believe it was a mistake that on the evening of the 8th of this month, our bank was broken into by thieves, who stole a total of over 900 yuan of silver and miscellaneous coins that had not yet been deposited in the treasury. We are afraid that the rumors will be untrue, so we ask you to correct the letter as appropriate. Yours sincerely, Puhai Bank of Minhang, January 14th.

To the Editor: I have read in your newspaper's local news column an article entitled "Japanese Exclude Chinese Seamen" with the news "Zheng Ji Employs Japanese People." It says that our company is now dismissing Chinese sailors one after another, successively hiring Japanese people to replace them, and that Wang Gongrang, the chief engineer of the Fuli wheel, has been suspended, and Japanese people have been forcibly sent to the ship, causing opposition from the crew. This is completely inconsistent with the facts. Our company has not only not dismissed Chinese sailors and hired Japanese people, but has also dismissed dozens of Japanese sailors since this year. The facts are clear and can be easily verified. However, Wang Gongrang's departure from the Fuli wheel was actually a crew transfer. The crew member refused to be transferred and resigned on his own. It was not the company's intention to suspend him. I am afraid that the outside world does not understand the truth, so I am writing to you to present the facts, hoping that you will correct them to clarify the truth. Sincerely, Zheng Ji Steamship Company, January 15th.

To the Editor: I read in today's newspaper that the Reuter's dispatch from Berlin on January 14 stated that the Friedrich Alfred factory, which closed today, is not located in Essen, but in Rheinhausen, not far from Duisburg. It is an old steel factory owned by Krupp. Recently, the company has built a new steel factory near Essen in Bochum to replace the old factory in Rheinhausen, so the old factory has been closed. Our bank is the manager of Krupp, and we are providing the facts. Sincerely, Lihe Foreign Bank.

To the Editor: I read in today's newspaper that I took the night train to Beijing last night. However, I am still in Shanghai and have not gone anywhere else. Moreover, because the government is thick-skinned and humiliating the country, and losing its sovereignty, I have not participated in party politics. I am afraid that the outside world does not understand the truth, so I am writing to you to clarify. Sincerely, He Xiangning, January 15th, noon.

Concerning Student Work 254

Bitter. Study. Save. The Nation. Miss. Yuan. Tou. Zhen.

Since the Japanese imperialists have inflicted their aggression and brutality upon our three northeastern provinces, the youth of our entire nation, stirred by righteous indignation and the surge of ardent blood, have spontaneously organized volunteer armies and rescue teams, sometimes departing to the front lines to serve. Others have formed groups for lecturing, posting slogans, distributing leaflets, and even petitioning in the capital as a whole. Finally, before the end of the semester, they have voluntarily suspended classes to engage in practical work. This practical work is still in its initial stages. Students from other provinces have already returned home for the New Year, and those in the local area have stopped attending school. Scattered in this way, how will the work actually progress? How should the work be done in the future? I think it will inevitably involve continuing efforts with strikes and petitions. However, I believe that, for practical work, strikes are absolutely unfeasible, and mass petitions are also unnecessary. Although the power of a mass petition is great, it is also fraught with danger. It would be such a pity to sacrifice valuable young people in vain. Our future nation depends on the righteousness of the youth. How should young students cherish themselves?

During this time of national crisis, the path our young students should take is to focus on their studies, advance step by step, recognize what China lacks and needs, accelerate their pursuit of knowledge, and conduct extensive research. I believe that the Chinese are not inherently untalented; they simply do not put in enough effort. For example, some of our young students study military affairs, some study politics, some study medicine, some study engineering, some study commerce, and some study education and mathematics. It can be said that there are students of all kinds. How many of them actually succeed in their studies? Most rely on political changes to create opportunities for employment, and many drop out of school halfway. How regrettable this is! We should now break this opportunism and strive for in-depth scholarship. At this critical moment of national crisis, we should work hard to study. Studying is not about being calm or not resisting; it is precisely the preparation for resistance. During this period, those studying military affairs should intensify their training and delve into tactics. Those studying politics should pay attention to diplomacy and observe the international situation, which is particularly important. Those studying medicine should practice. Those studying engineering should research manufacturing, aiming to make inventions in weaponry and machinery that surpass other countries. Those studying commerce should study international trade. Those studying education should research how to lead young people. Those studying mathematics and chemistry should bury themselves in deep thought and go to the laboratories. Our lack of scientific knowledge is well known and should be particularly emphasized. Those studying agriculture should study farming. Those studying art should widely promote literature and posters to make everyone understand the Japanese aggression and brutality. They should also compose songs to inspire people. We know that China does not lack soldiers; we do not need everyone to become a soldier. We only need everyone to fulfill their respective roles and responsibilities. In the inevitable time of war, our soldiers will fight on the front lines, and the accumulation of food in the rear will depend on the development of agriculture. The supply of military equipment will depend on the rapid and excellent manufacturing. The treatment of the wounded will rely on the skillful surgeries of doctors. The transmission of military information will rely on the completeness of transportation. Furthermore, transportation and newspapers, etc., all require the design of our specialized scholars, which is the responsibility of our young students. How can we easily abandon what we have learned? Only through diligent study can we save the nation. Striving to study is our effective work. (Ding)
