Small Forum

We Should Support the Righteous and Brave Army 256

丨丨 Because this is the people's own military force. China has raised more than two million soldiers. Including all local militias, police, and irregular troops, the total number must be over three million. According to the Ministry of Finance, the military expenditure required for regular troops each year already accounts for 80% of the total financial expenditure. Combining this with other local defense expenses and various levies, the enormous figure is even more shocking. However, such a huge military expenditure is only used to support warlords as pawns, seize power, and extract the blood and flesh of the people, causing endless internal strife for the past twenty years. We can say that our country has no national military force, no people's military force, but only a military force that serves individuals and brings disaster to the country and people.

When the disaster in the Northeast broke out, Zhang Xueliang strictly ordered the Northeast Army not to resist. Within a few days, half of the Northeast was lost. When the Japanese army attacked Longjiang, General Ma Zhanshan fought alone. Zhang Xueliang again remained inactive, sending not a single soldier to help. As a result, Longjiang fell. When the Japanese army attacked Jinzhou, Zhang Xueliang ordered the troops stationed in Jinzhou to retreat entirely into the customs without fighting back. Instead, he used the excuse that the central government did not provide ammunition or sufficient pay, and sent a telegram saying, "I do not want to be a political sacrifice." Such foolish, weak, and power-hungry soldiers, such negligent and unpatriotic officials, deserve to die ten thousand times over.

As for the troops in the provinces within the customs, they are also merely tools of individuals, only knowing how to point their guns inward. When foreign enemies are approaching and the country is being torn apart, they turn a deaf ear. The people are squeezed for their blood and sweat to support the army, but the army only brings disaster to the country and people. This phenomenon is truly heartbreaking and a clear lesson for us.

Since the fall of the three northeastern provinces, righteous and brave armies have sprung up everywhere, attacking the Japanese army everywhere, making the enemy exhausted. In the Battle of Jinzhou, the stationed troops retreated entirely, but the righteous and brave army fought desperately, firmly defending the city. Eventually, they were outnumbered and Jinzhou inevitably fell. Recently, in the area around Dahu Mountain, they have repeatedly inflicted heavy losses on the enemy. According to yesterday's news, they have even recaptured Dahu Mountain. The momentum of the righteous and brave army is extremely strong. These facts and actions are truly worthy of praise and tears, and represent the hope of our entire nation!

The righteous and brave army is the people's own military force. Only the people's own military force can resist tyranny and defend against foreign aggression, and only then can we save ourselves and the country. Only when the people organize themselves, arm themselves, and take on the responsibility of saving the country can the country be saved. Hoping for others is like quenching thirst with plums; it is ultimately futile.

Therefore, we should now earnestly support the righteous and brave armies fighting hard in various parts of the Northeast, giving them spiritual encouragement and material assistance. At the same time, the people in various regions should especially organize themselves and prepare to use their own military force to defeat the military force of the imperialists and all evil forces. Only in this way can China have a way out, and only then can the suffering people of China have a way out.

Popular Literature and Art

A Rare Death A Humble Opinion 257

"Death" is not rare, because "all men must die." However, I consider the death of my friend He Mo to be "rare." This is of course not because he was my friend, but because he was also a "person," and a pure young person.

In these troubled times, "speaking" and "writing articles" must be done carefully. This is true. However, He Mo never said "unpleasant words," nor did he write "articles that should not be written." He sat in his room reading all day long. Who knew that "disaster descends from the sky even when one sits in a room"? He Mo was suddenly arrested and imprisoned. The crime for which he was imprisoned was said to be the discovery of several books on the study of scientific socialism on his desk.

"Truth" has long resided under the eaves of those in authority. He Mo actually fantasized about finding truth in books. That is of course an unforgivable crime, and "violates" the "law." Therefore, he easily obtained a rose-colored crown.

Unfortunately, He Mo was also a poor boy. He had nothing good to stuff the dog hole. The dog hole was not stuffed, so the dog would naturally come out and bite people. Therefore, He Mo suffered multiple tortures after being imprisoned.

This pure young man had only a candid heart. I know that he had neither made a revolution nor opposed a revolution, or reformed a revolution.

The death of a revolutionary is "achieving benevolence," and the death of a counter-revolutionary is "being executed." Logically, since He Mo was not qualified to "achieve benevolence," he would naturally not be "executed." Therefore, he was sentenced to one year and six months of imprisonment between being unclear about whether he was guilty or innocent.

In the iron window like a beast cage, He Mo was almost sick for a year. Before his imprisonment period was over, his illness became heavier day by day. There was no doctor to diagnose him and no medicine to take. A person who has "violated" the "law" "should" die, let alone just be sick?

The prisoners in the same prison as He Mo, watching his illness become serious, felt a little sad. They asked the prison guard to remove the iron shackles from his feet, because he had long been unable to move. After a few more days, the prison officer discovered that this dying prisoner really did not need to be shackled, so he ordered the prison guard to remove them. The two prison guards carried He Mo out of the prison gate and kindly removed his shackles! The shackles were removed, and the person died!

Because He Mo was "not guilty of his crime," he was unwilling to die with iron shackles? When I heard the news of his death, I did not shed tears for him. I just did not understand, because this was a "rare death."

Popular Science

Method of Producing Light Gas Ding Xi 258

Take a basin, fill it with clean water, and then use pliers to take a piece of sodium. The molecular formula of sodium is Na, which is a metal element. It easily combines with air, so it must be immersed in kerosene when not in use to prevent it from combining with air and burning. Next, use scissors to cut the sodium into many small pieces, but each piece should not be too large; because if it is too large, it may explode when it burns in water. Then wrap each small piece of sodium in paper, but do not wrap it too tightly; because if it is wrapped too tightly, the light gas will be difficult to come out when it is placed in water. When wrapping the sodium in paper, be careful not to get the sodium on your hands, to avoid skin ulcers. After these procedures are completed, fill a test tube or a larger glass bottle with water, press the mouth of the tube tightly with the palm of your right hand, and turn it upside down in the water in the basin. Use your left hand to lift the tube, but do not lift it out of the water; because if it is lifted out of the water, the outside air will get in and drive out the water in the tube. Then, use the pliers in your right hand to clamp the paper-wrapped sodium one piece at a time under the mouth of the test tube. Once the sodium is clamped into the water, it will immediately decompose the water and turn into sodium hydroxide (molecular formula is NaOH), releasing hydrogen (molecular formula is H) that rises into the test tube and drives the water down. After the water in the tube is completely driven out, use a piece of glass to tightly cover the mouth of the bottle in the water, then take it out and turn it upside down on the table. Because light gas is lighter than air, it may rise and escape, so it must be placed upside down on the table. But even if it is upside down, the glass cover must not be removed. Then, gradually move the bottle up, and send a lit match into the mouth of the tube, which will emit a faint explosion. If a burning candle is sent into the mouth of the tube, a burning flame will be seen at the mouth of the tube, but the candle flame will be extinguished in the tube. This proves that light gas can burn in the air and does not have combustion-supporting properties.

Street Sociology

Various Ways of Life (3) Xingzi 259

On Edward Road, Tibet Road, and other relatively wide roads, you can always appreciate the unique "street literature."

These articles are mostly written on the road with chalk. Some are in Chinese, some are in Western languages. The Chinese ones include parallel prose, prose, ancient styles, and seven-character and five-character quatrains. As for the characters, many are written extremely vigorously and elegantly.

"I, a person from × place, graduated from ××× school at an early age, and then taught at × place. Due to bad luck and a family robbery, I am plagued by illness and have fallen into Shanghai. Relatives and friends are cut off, and I am whipped by hunger and cold. A man's spirit is short, and the money by the bed is exhausted. A strong man has no face, so Wu Yuan cannot but play the flute in the Wu market, and Feng Xuan cannot but pluck the sword at the Hou's gate. It is a last resort, and it is doubly heartbreaking. I dare to ask benevolent gentlemen to pity my situation and generously donate to revive the dried fish. I will definitely repay you one day. The afflicted person ××× tearfully begs."

This is one example. Beside this lingering and tragic "mourning notice," there are often one or two seven-character quatrains, five-character quatrains, or seven-character or five-character regulated verses.

"Drifting in Shanghai year after year, I look to the sky with white eyes;

Who recognizes the flute player in the Wu market? I can't bear to shed tears before you."

This is also an example. For example:

"The sun sets cold on the Wu River, and the sky is cold with crows flying in the evening;

May I ask the flute player: Whose house will you stay in tonight?"

This is another example. As for English, there is "I am a teacher of":

"Ma nataye Country is"

The writers of this kind of literature include men and women. Sometimes women bring one or two children with them. They always have an attitude of "resentment without anger, sorrow without pain" and look around at the audience with pleading eyes. There are often several places on a road. If you are a newcomer to Shanghai, you will definitely wonder if this is an "open-air literature exhibition."

What they fear most is the scenery-spoiling patrolman. When they spot a patrolman coming, they quietly walk away.

Southeast Northwest

"Monte Carlo" Yi Xin 260

"Monte Carlo" is a famous casino in Monaco, France. Those who go there to gamble are all high-ranking officials and wealthy people, because they have nothing to do all day long, so they gather there to gamble heavily.

In order to establish a large casino in Monaco, they, the casino operators, gave 400,000 pounds to the Prince of Monaco. This was in 1899. Later, in 1913, they gave him another 600,000 pounds, plus an annual rent of 50,000 pounds, and an additional 10,000 pounds every ten years until the end of the lease. Although they have to pay such an astonishing amount of money every year, they still think it is very profitable. Then who are the losers? Needless to say, it is the people who go there to gamble.

Shanghai is now becoming the second "Monte Carlo" quickly. Many women in high society go to casinos to gamble, and there are quite a few casinos, especially in the × concession, where even very famous people can be found. What is their purpose in going there? This is self-evident, but wealth is in the hands of fate and cannot be forced. Have you ever seen anyone become rich by gambling? Even if luck comes temporarily and they actually win, it will soon be a bubble. It comes from there and goes back there. The so-called "goods enter with a burst and also go out with a burst" is certain. In the end, they still try to steal a chicken but lose the rice. The saying "If you want to get rich, you must have bad luck" is really not wrong. Therefore, "gambling" is not a way to make money. Only "diligence" and "frugality" are the real ways to make money. (1.11 Lamp)

Small Consumption Statistics 261

— Xu Shui Lin

× Prostitutes

There are approximately 100,000 prostitutes in this city, including "number two," "long three," "wild chickens," and those leading similar lives of prostitution. The direct and indirect living expenses required per person per day are approximately 1.20 yuan.

The total daily amount is 120,000 yuan.

The total monthly amount is 3.6 million yuan.

The total annual amount is 43.2 million yuan.

If there are 200,000 people, the total annual amount would be 86.4 million yuan.

If there are 300,000 people, the total amount would be 130 million yuan.

Plus 25% for luxury expenses, amounting to 32.5 million yuan.

Adding this to the previous total, the total is 162.5 million yuan.

Shanghai Story

Shanghai Story (11) Compiled and Translated by Zhou Rong 262

× The Establishment of the American Concession

According to H. B. Morse in his book "The International Relations of the Chinese Empire," the establishment of the American Concession was not created by human effort, but rather developed naturally. This statement makes a lot of sense. Because the merchants in the concession wanted to find cheap land for their residences, they bought land in the suburbs near the concession. The American Episcopal Church began to buy land and build churches in Hongkou. In Xianfeng four years (February 1854), the first American consul arrived in Shanghai and hoisted the American flag in the concession before the American Concession had even been demarcated.

The bishop of the American Episcopal Church was William J. Boone.

He asked the American consul to designate the southern boundary of the church. The American consul said that the small road along the river in front of the church would be the boundary. As a result, the Suzhou River bank belonged to the Episcopal Church.

Initially, neither the American Concession nor the French Concession were prosperous places.

Later, the missionaries of the Jesus Church found a new site near the concession. The cornerstone of the Dongjiadu Catholic Church was laid on the 21st day of the 11th month of Daoguang twenty-eighth year.

Initially, the status of American expatriates was not very good, and even the American consul's desire to set up a consulate in the British Concession aroused the British's antipathy. It can be seen that the reason why the consuls of the United States and France asked the Chinese authorities to open another concession was actually because the British monopolized the British Concession, forcing them to open another concession to accommodate expatriates from the United States and France.

In fact, whether they were British, Americans, or French, they did not feel discriminated against by each other and were very harmonious, because they knew that their interests were the same: they were all imperialists who came to trample on Chinese soil and did not need to squeeze each other out! Therefore, in Tongzhi two years (1863), the British and American concessions were actually merged to form the current Public Concession.

Random Notes

New Trends in Divorce Procedures in Various Countries Fu Lan 263

Postal divorces in Mexico have become popular nationwide recently. In addition, secret divorces can also be decided and approved by judges. As for cases that do not require debate, applicants do not even need to state the reasons specifically when submitting the petition.

Oklahoma, Arizona, and Idaho are particularly convenient for divorce. They have lenient laws, understanding judges, and even Arkansas, which uses hot springs as a divorce colony. Before submitting the petition, a residence of sixty days is required, and after submitting the petition, another thirty days of residence is required to wait for the final verdict to be issued. In Cuba, those requesting a divorce only need to reside for thirty days.

The divorce laws of Morelos state in Mexico are considered the simplest and easiest to achieve the purpose. Although the Mexican High Court ruled not long ago that anti-divorce in Morelos state is not effective outside the state, foreigners still rely on the help of lawyers and judges to come here to cancel their marriage contracts. Some states in Mexico have no divorce laws, and some states believe that there is no need for such laws. In many Mexican courts, the divorce petitions submitted are almost the same, with incompatibility or mutual consent as reasons, but most of them are unreliable. Since 1912, even the most hard-hearted Mexicans have been shocked by their postal divorces. Today, everyone is used to it and does not find it strange. The procedure is very simple. If one party wants a divorce, they only need to publish a notice in the newspaper. If the other party does not see this notice, it is their own loss. After the verdict is issued, a copy of the notice is sent to the other party, and the matter is completed.

Even the Chinese, who are under patriarchal society, have opened up a divorce avenue. According to the report of the Social Bureau last year, there were 853 divorce cases in Shanghai, 809 in Peiping, and 226 in Guangzhou. Divorce mainly occurs among foreigners and educated Chinese, while those who silently abide by the old etiquette and old ideas still dare not try it.

Russia still holds the record for swift divorces. There is a divorce bureau in any big city or town. Either party can apply for a divorce without stating the reason or notifying the other party. In fact, the required procedure takes only five minutes. Therefore, a large line of people often stands in front of the window of the divorce bureau, waiting for half an hour to get what they want. Because Russian law does not allow counterclaims and defenses, there is no need for judges or lawyers. It is neither expensive nor delayed, so it is no wonder that Russians flock to it. If there are children, the issue of alimony must be determined within three days after the divorce. The court will rule which party will raise the children, which party will be responsible for the alimony, and how much alimony should be paid. In some places, when there is no legal provision for alimony, it is borne jointly by both men and women, but in reality, wives rarely pay. In one hundred divorce cases with children, children are assigned to the mother in 95% of the cases. According to observers, the divorce rate in Russia in the first year of marriage is five times higher than in the United States, but after ten years of marriage, their rate of breaking up couples is only twice as high as in the United States.

In the courts of old Russia, if a complete divorce case was tried, solemn regalia had to be displayed, and two monks and two or more pastors had to rush from Moscow and St. Petersburg to participate in the trial and conduct a long-term investigation of the case. Today, however, one person stuffs a piece of paper out of a window hole, and the divorce procedure is completed.

Before 1916 in Turkey, husbands had the right to drive out his wife at any time without notice. Conversely, women had to appear in court and prove their allegations before obtaining a divorce. But since the Young Turk movement and the establishment of the new country, the law has been amended to give women extra convenience, explaining that marriage is a joint contract between men and women. Currently, Turkish women can enjoy all the rights that men enjoy in marriage, including the right to divorce. According to scholars, Islamic law, except for marriage and divorce, often treats women more favorably than general Western codes. However, they are now being amended to ensure that women receive the same wages as men, and whether married or unmarried, they can choose any job.

This summer, India promulgated new divorce regulations. From then on, Indian women can divorce their husbands because of laziness, refusal to support, frequent bad tempers, or unchaste behavior.

Although the divorce procedures in various countries are becoming simpler, some countries still refuse to accept them. Brazil does not recognize divorce at all, and does not recognize bigamy as legal. It is said that Rio de Janeiro is currently drafting a divorce law, all based on the United States. Also, according to the recent regulations of a certain cathedral, any person whose previous marriage has been declared terminated by a civil court and invalidated by a monk can be married by the pastor of the cathedral, as if they had never been married before.

Although Belgium is a Catholic country, it has recognized divorce since 1830. Today, the Netherlands allows foreigners to reside for three months to enjoy the convenience of divorce.

Market News 264

Letter from Lily Motor Company: The Lily & Co. Motor Company on Suzhou Road in this city has received one hundred of the latest American-style automobiles. All are painted with checkerboard markings, specially for the needs of temporary business trips. Utilizing scientific management methods, they are available on call, charging only one dollar for every twenty minutes.

Letter from Sino-Western Dispensary: The Sino-Western Dispensary on Shanghai's Fourth Avenue, as well as its two branches on Zhejiang Road and the Xiaodongmen and Nanshi areas of Central Shanghai, are simultaneously holding a special grand sale with large giveaways for three weeks. In addition to selling all goods at discounted prices, "Rose Fragrance Honey," "Hundred Flower Fragrance Powder," and portraits of the famous sixteen-year-old young lady are prepared as gifts.

Letter from Calligrapher Chen Xinzhi: Recently, to promote the art of calligraphy amongst all sectors, I am offering a fifty percent reduction in my fees starting today. Detailed examples are available. Enclose two cents postage for a prompt reply. Correspondence address: Xinzhizhou Book Residence, No. 2069, Jingxing Lane, Dongyouheng Road, Shanghai.

Letter from the Liuyin Painting Exhibition: The Liuyin Society's Chinese painting exhibition, organized by Wang Zhongshan, Zhang Yuguang, Xu Xiaochun, and others, opened to the public yesterday (the 14th) at the Ningbo Fellow-Provincials Association on Tibet Road.
